After I have finished this for you, O Children, a book which is the last knowledge in medicine with its completion, and I have reached the end of it through its explanations and its declarations, it was my wish to complete it for you with this treatise which is a part of the operation, that is, chirugery with my hand.
Because the operation with the hand is laid low in our region and completely cut off: until perhaps science of it perishes, and its track is abolished: and they do not remain except brief descriptions in ancient books, which have changed their hands: and an error and hesitation happen to them until their intentions are closed, and the length of its will is elongated: It seemed good to me to enliven it with the life of this treatise in it according to the way of position and declaration and abbreviation: and to make it like the forms of the Cauteries and other instruments of work: when an addition is made to the declaration, and the operation of its being necessary is performed.
However, the cause why this good craftsman did not find it with his hand in our time is: because medicine is long, and it is necessary for the author to exercise before that in the knowledge of anatomy which Galen narrated, until he knows the humors of the members, and their forms, and their connection, and their separation, and has knowledge of bones, and nerves, and tendons, and the number of them, and their exit, and the pulsatility and quietness, and the exits of their places:
And therefore Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little, and especially in the art of the hand:
But we have already spoken of that at the beginning of this book:
Because he who is not knowledgeable of what I say about anatomy does not understand, but already falls into error, wherein men are slain: as I have seen many of them, who are formed from this science, and cast it aside without knowledge, and without experiment.
That which is, because I have seen a stupid physician cut the abscess of a woman's neck, and some arteries were cut in her neck: therefore blood flowed from the woman until she died at his hands.
And I have seen another physician, who presumed to extract a stone from a boy who had grown up, and the stone was large. Therefore he went to him, and extracted it with a small instrument. And the boy died on the third day.
Indeed I had called to extract it myself: and I saw from the greatness of the stone, and the weakness of the position, that he would die.
And I have seen another physician, who received a stipe from a certain Duke of our land for medicine: and it happened to an eunuch black man, who was near the heel of his wrist, and he broke: and the physician, not knowing his own ignorance, struck the fracture with his thumb over the ulna with pulsars, and strong bows, and did not release the wound's expiration.
Then he released him according to his desire. Later he released him for days, and warned him not to loosen the bandage: and he stood thus until the abscess of his foot was out, and his own leg, and he called for death.
I am called to him: and I came to loosen the bandage: and peace followed, and he was freed from his pains.
Indeed, corruption had already been confirmed in the member and I could not halt it.
When corruption ceased to walk in the member, it has now perished.
And I saw another physician who had pierced an epidermoid cancer: the ulcer has worsened over days until his malice was fully revealed to the lord of it.
What this means is that when the cancer is pure from the melancholic fluid, it does not need to be treated with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can tolerate it, so that the entirety of it can be amputated.
And therefore, O Son, it is necessary for you to know that the operation is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation associated with safety, and the operation with which there is danger in many arrangements.
And I have already stirred up the entirety of this book, in which the operation comes where there is terror and fear.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to guard against this, and let it go: so that foolish people may not find it to speak, and to dishonor.
Therefore, take the measure with anxiety and protection, and your weakness with ease and firmness, and use it as a better means of salvation and praiseworthy succession by the grace of God: and let go of difficult-to-heal terrifying afflictions, and remove your spirits from that which makes you fear, so that it may come upon you a doubt in your faith and comfort.
For it is more remaining for your glory, and sublime in this world, and finally for your quantities.
Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat illness with evil: do not call physicians bad.
However, this treatise is divided into three chapters.
Chapter first.
Chapter on cauterization with fire and sharp-edged medicine, divided into sections from the head to the feet, and descriptions of the tools and instruments of cauterization, and all that is necessary for the operation.
Chapter second.
Chapter on sections and piercings, bloodletting and venting, and wounds: and the removal of arrows and similar, and all the chapter is divided into forms of instruments.
Chapter third.
Chapter on restoration, and dislocation, and curing of twisting, and similar: the chapter is divided from the head to the feet, and descriptions of the tools and instruments.
However, before that, it is necessary to say about the quality of the wounds and the effects of cauterization of his own: and in which complexion it will be shown.
I say that the speech about the quality of cauterization and its effects is a long and subtle one, knowledge, and a secret and hidden science.
Even many wise men have spoken about it, and they have disputed about it, and for me it is enough a little from their words, fearing the extension.
I say that cauterization is effective against all wounds, whether with matter or without matter, except for two wounds: the hot wound without matter and the dry wound without matter.
However, in the hot and dry wound with matter, they differ. Some have said that cauterization is in the hot and dry wound with matter. However, others have said that cauterization is not suitable for the disease which is from heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable to heal from a hot and dry disease with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite has said that by cauterization a wound is made in all hot and dry disease that occurs in the bodies of humans: for when you compare the body of a man and its humors to the fire, you will find the body of a man cold.
I myself say by his words: because I have already experienced this by experiment.
Nevertheless, it does not belong for him to come upon that, unless he who has already proved it, and has been exercised in the chapter of cauterization, and has known the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of diseases in themselves, and their causes, and accidents, and the space of time of theirs.
However, there is no fear from the rest of the complexions: and especially in cold and humid diseases. For all physicians have come to them, and they have not differed in the wound with cauterization in them.
And you know, O sons, that by the secret of the curing with Cauterization with fire, and the goodness of it over the medicine burning with Cauterization is: for fire is simple, whose action does not affect anything except to the member which is cauterized, and does not hurt another member connected with it, unless it hurts a little.
The action of burning surgeons in medicine is directed towards that which is extended from the limbs: and perhaps it causes difficulty in the treatment of difficult disease in a member, and perhaps it kills.
However, fire, because of its own subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless it is superfluous.
Indeed, we have learned this by experiment, because of the length of the servitude and study with the art, and the station above the truth of things: and for that reason I excuse the length of the speech.
And if there were not, because it is not allowed for this book of mine to bring you the secret, hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies, by which it expels diseases that are demonstrated in the philosophical speech, which is disturbed by your minds.
And do you know, sons, that you yourself dissent in the time when it is fitting to make the cauterization, and you set a better time for the lesson.
And I say that cauterization is fitting in every time, because the harm done by the time is swallowed up in the wound, which is attracted by the cauterization. And above all, if the cauterization is made for necessary pains, which are hard, urgent, which do not endure delay: for that reason, because it is feared that a greater evil may happen than the small harm that is done by the time.
And it will not fall into your sons' minds that this is not true, unless they are foolish and stupid physicians, namely that the diseases which are cured by cauterization are not always a return: and they set this as a consequence, and the thing is not as they think: for cauterization is not but in the place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and dries up the humors which are causes of the pains, therefore the pains happen.
Indeed, cauterization benefits the patient's health, its own virtue, and the vigor of his dominion. It is possible that the illness leaves for a certain period of time according to the complexion of the weak, and the location of the patient's illness, and the virtue of his illness. And that it is prepared in the body of him from the aggregation of superfluities in him. And that it is sated with it in its acquisition from foods, and similar ones from like causes, unless an illness occurs, in which the cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in the member of a few superfluities and moistures, like the cauterization of teeth, for pain, and such like, is possible that it does not remain in that pain. But that happens in few.
But that speech is a true saying: not to what they intend in it: for they believe that there is no cure which confers with the medicine, nor with another after the occasion of the cauterization.
But the case is opposite to that, and the intention, that cauterization is the last of the medicines, is not, unless when we administer modes of cure in some illnesses, and they do not conform to the medicine: then we administer the cauterization at the end of the disease, and it conforms: then it falls out that cauterization is the last of the medicines, not according to the intention which wise and experienced physicians understand.
But the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than with iron: and they did not say this except for the equality of gold, and the sublimity of its own substance: and they said that it does not make a pus in the place of the cauterization. Indeed, that is not entirely true: for I have already proven that, and found that it does not make that in certain bodies without others.
And cauterization, when used alone, is good, and better than when iron is used, as they say. However, when you use fire for cauterization on gold, it is not declared to you when it is heated according to the amount you wish, because of the redness of the gold: and when it approaches the cold, and if you add more heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into layers.
Therefore, the artisan falls away from that occupation: and therefore cauterization is made with iron among us, more easily and nearer, due to the straightness to the operation.
And I have indeed ordered this chapter on cauterization, according to the chapter: and I have ordered them from the head down to the feet: so that they may be sought by those who wish to find out what is in it.
Head 2.
This cauterization is applied to the mastery of moisture and coldness over the head: which are two causes of salt, and the multitude of fluids from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the multitude of dreams, and pain of teeth, and pain of the throat: and generally all kinds of disease that happen from coldness, such as paralysis, and salt, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar ones from those diseases.
The method of cauterization is to apply it to the weak: so that it may be emptied in the beginning with the dissolved medicine of the head three or four nights, according to the strength of the infirm, and their age, and their habit.

And some of them said that it should be cauterized to the bone, and hold the cauterization until it becomes thick with some density of bones.
Then it is shaved after that which has been made thick from the bone, and then it is cured.

I do not recognize these two kinds of cauterization at all, except in some men according to their fear.
And to let it go, in my opinion, is better with the health of the patient.
The head weakens from the solution of its own continuous nature, as we have testified in other parts of the body: and especially when the head is feeble and weak in nature: and the first kind of cauterization is indeed safer and better with me, and I use it: therefore, to operate with this in health.
¶ The Head (III).
When there is a chronic pain throughout the head, and it lasts in the feeble, and uses leeches, and needles, and head pills, and oils, and plasters: And especially if it has already been cauterized with the iron we have mentioned, and nothing benefits it from these: then consider. For if the head is weak from a strong nature of creation, and it is not feeble, and it finds cold weather: then cauterize with another iron less than that. Then cauterize it over the whole of its own head with the iron, and do not pierce the skin, and do not cut through the quantity of bone which we have mentioned. He should cauterize himself with a single burn on the back of his head, in the place known as the 'vagina'. This is the place where the wind is produced, and he should cut away the hair of his face, and not neglect the bone. For he is weak because of this painful grief, and it differs from the pain of other head cauteries.
And I say this: and it is necessary that this be the cauterization in its place: and it should be the cauterization whereby the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of his head with a softer cauterization, whereby the middle of the head is cauterized.
Head IV.
When pain and swelling occur in a part of the head, or it extends to the eye, and the face becomes moist with the application of medicines, and the rest of the treatment is given as I said in the divisions of illness, and it does not fit all of this: then the cauterization in him is of two kinds: either with hot medicine burning: or with iron.
But when the cauterization is with hot medicine burning, it is like this: take a tooth from another person, and encircle it, and cut off the ends of its sides. Then divide the place of pain when the phlebitis is wide, until there is a place under the skin where the tooth can be caught.
Then insert it into the same place under the skin until it is hidden: then tie it around with a suitable string, and release it after fifteen hours, then extract the tooth, and remove the almond, and leave it for two or three days, or four: then place a submerged belly over the place, until the place produces pus: then care for it with ointment until it is healed.

§ About the method of cauterizing in pain of the ear.

And this is the form of cauterization, and it is a species from the penknife, whose form we have mentioned: verily it is not too thin, as you see: and it is necessary that the penknife be in it with too much bulk.

On the method of cauterization in paralysis and mollification.
Chapter 10.
It is necessary to proceed with the cleaning of the head with hot water and as said before.
Then rub the weak head: then cauterize it with cauterization in the middle of the head, and with cauterization over all the crown, and with cauterization over the posterior part of it, and three over the spine of the neck.
However, if you need more than one cauterization for the mollification of the body, and the patient tolerates it well, and the disease is strong: then cauterize it with four cauterizations over the spine of the back, and the last one with cauterization until it burns most of its skin, and use your hand to peel it off. Then take care of it until it heals: and then apply olive oil.
On the method of cauterization in epilepsy.
Epilepsy is not cauterized unless it belongs to someone with a phlegmatic epilepsy.
Therefore, it is necessary to clean the head of his brain first with hot water and as said before with the rest of the care that I mentioned in division, when he is weak or tolerates in acceptance of the medicine.
However, if the child is one who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and mastications are given to clean the head of his brain before that days with many good foods.
Then rub his head, then cauterize it with one cauterization in the middle of the head, according to how it precedes in the way: and with another cauterization on the back of his head, and over all the crown of his own cauterization. That if he is weak but tolerates it well, then cauterize him with the cauterizations I said in having paralysis and mollification of the body over the spine of the neck, and over the spine of the back: and let the olive oil be a cauterization according to the way that precedes.
If then the boy is weak, place a fine cauterium at that time. So.
On the method of cauterization in melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupt humors and a gross phlegm, then cauterize it with the cauteries we have mentioned for paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is superfluous humors that turn to melancholy, and the body is a moist one, then give it power to cleanse its brain according to what precedes in division: then shave the head of the infirm one, and afterward make a decent tortellum from linen, as a circle.
Then place it on the middle of the head: and the infirm one sitting squarely is held from all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is more suitable from ancient honey. And heat it over a tempered fire with the measured heat of the fingers, when it is inserted into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of its head in a circle, and release it until it is hardened.
Do this to the weak one once a week, with the good rule of the remaining, until it is cured.
Or if you will, cauterize it by making small points on it as much as possible, besides holding the hand with the cauterization, and let it be fragrant.
For this species of cauterization moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place over it the drunk one that has swallowed the honey or goose fat.
Chapter XIII. On the method of cauterization in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When I declare to you the beginning of water in the eye through the signs which I said in division, then begin to drink the weak water, with that which cleanses its head.

If you see something from it, then cut him off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I am like with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting, and caution of the flow of blood.
And when it is cauterized in the hair, under two bones, with the last two cauteries.
¶ About the way of cauterizing in ancient tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and frequent: and they are over the veins, and the arteries which are in the manifest skin of the head: it is believed that this is from superfluous cold, and phlegmatic: then cauterize with the same cauterization that I will tell you about the delay of water descending, with cauterization in the middle of the head, and two cauteries over two times, and two cauteries in the hair under two bones. And if you need an addition, then cauterize it on all sides of the eye, with a small cauterization at the end of the eyebrow.
In a similar manner, cauterization is performed on the beard of the nose.
When you are treating this, if the division is as we have said and there is no need for medication, then immediately give three doses of the ointment to an impoverished patient: then shave the head of the patient and cauterize it with a medium-sized cauterizing iron, using olive oil. Then cauterize it with the cauterizing iron using two cauterizing irons, over two above the eyebrows, under the very short hair.
And guard against the artery, do not set it on fire.
This is the form of Clauilis cauterization.
In a similar manner, cauterization is performed on the eyelid for smoothing.
When the eyelid is smoothed by disease or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cauterizing iron, using the moon-shaped cauterizing iron.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows with two cauterizing irons in all parts: and they will elongate in two intervals: and the length of the cauterization should be according to the length of the eyebrows, and not finally your hand with the cauterizing iron, even according to the amount that becomes third eyelid.
In a similar manner, cauterization is performed on the eyelid when the hairs become rough and painful in the eye.
The cauterizing iron in this is according to two methods: either with fire, or with a burning medicine.
In cauterization with fire, you should advise the patient beforehand to let go of his hairs, if he has them shaved, until they grow out and become longer. If, however, they prick him at his own point: then bind his eyes with thread, so that they may not move, until they are born.
When they are born and turn, then place the weak head in the fold of your garment: then make a sign on the eyelids of his eyes with a candle, a sign that is according to the figure of the myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the sign be near the hair.
Then place a drunken mouth on the aliment: or on the eye with a silk mucilage.
Then burn the cauterization, whose form is this.
Then cauterize over the figure which you have gradually marked on many skin folds, until the surface of the skin is completely burned, which is like the figure of the myrtle leaf, in its entirety.
And the sign of your healing work is: if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting, and the hair being plucked at the point of the eye.
Then pluck out your hand: and let it be three days.
Then place a drunken mouth on the aliment with honey, until the scar is eradicated. Then care for it with ointment, until it is healed.
If any hair remains after the hour, and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat the cauterization on that place, as you have done at first.
If the hairs are at the bottom: then cauterize it itself, until the hair becomes to its natural place, and is equal to not pricking the eye with a hair.
It is as if you were making a weak man free, until the hairs grow out and become long. The shape of the leaves of the myrtle tree on a sheet of paper.
Then take from the soap known, and from the unsoaked shoe, one ounce of weight, or almost the same: then dry it together with good contrition, and make it with haste, so that it does not fail. Then take from the pan and place it on the sheet of paper you made, like the shape of the myrtle leaf, and place it directly on the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a wet morsel, and make the weak head sit in your groove.
Then place your finger on the medicine and press it slightly. And move it as often as the weak feels the medicine's sting, for its sting is like fire.
While he persisted in this which he found to be the sting, then let him release the medicine, and move it with your finger. When the sting has ceased, then remove the medicine, and wash out the eye with water.
And then consider if you see the eyelid swelling up, as it does when contracting with fire or with incision, and that is good: and if not, then try again on the same spot of the medicine, until the operation of your hand has equalized and the eye has contracted.
Then place the wet morsel on top of it, until the scaly skin is burned away. Then care for it with ointment or other, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to keep the last watch, so that nothing falls out of the medicine into the eye.
That is if the eyelid becomes softened after a day, and something falls out of the hair into the eye, then try the medicine again on the same spot that was softened from the eyelid properly, as you did at first. Then take care of it itself until it is healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And you know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and proportions. Therefore, according to this, your consideration is: and the straightness of his desire for this art is not concealed.
¶ About the method of cauterizing in the tear duct.
When you are treating the tear duct fistula, when as we said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not agree with it: then, it is necessary for you to cauterize it according to this method.
Please make the patient place his head in your groove, and hold his head gently between his hands in this way, so that it does not move, nor does he move with his head.
Then place the injected cotton in the corner of the eye, or in the silica gel above his eye: then heat the cauterization, whose form is this.
Let it be thin, as the desired form of the pen of a quill wants to be from one end, with which the cauterization is made: and if you want it to pass through to the other end, and if you want it to be upward, then try.
However, this thinness is better for your work.

¶ About the method of cauterization in tooth pain.

Then dip it in the boiled grease: and place it over the painful tooth as soon as possible, and hold it until it strengthens: then repeat it several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip the wool, or the fire in cold grease, and place it over the painful tooth: and place a hot iron over it until the heat of the fire reaches the deep part of the tooth.

And this is the form of the cauterization.

In the manner of cauterizing the epar cold.

§ Method of Cauterization in Sciatica.

And beware in all your cauterizations that you do not always burn the nerve or the great artery with the cauterization, and do not harm the weak one with it, or cause a contraction.

Then take the dry dung of a goat, and burn it in the fire until it becomes charcoal.

De cauterizatione doloris Dorsi.
When a pain occurs in the back from various causes, or by chance, or by impact, or excessive evacuation, and such things, from cold and wet infusion: and cauterization indeed does not happen, unless in this very form, which is made from cold and wet infusion.
Therefore, after the evacuation of the weak, with pills that are fetid and such like, it should be made over the back where the pain is, three lines according to the breadth of the treated part, after which signs are made with encaustic in every line five cauteries, or more according to the tolerance of the weak power of this part, and cauterization should be made with cauteriopuncti.
And if you wish, cauterization should be made with three or four cauteries, or more, with the cauterio closed medially, according to this form.
De modo cauterizandi in incaeptine Gibbositatis.
This type of illness often affects infants in childbirth.
And the sign of its onset in boys is: that it occurs upon a stricture in the ankle during evacuation, and motion; and I found in the last vertebra of the back and the nodes of his, which has already begun to emerge above the others.
When you see this, and you want to do this, then cauterize it with the cauterization that is a circle according to this form.
And let the cauterization catch all parts of the vertebra equally: and if you want to cauterize in the circumference of the vertebra with the cauterization point two lines, or three: and they should be points close to the emerging one.
Then take care of the place until it heals with that which I said.
And be careful not to give the cauterization in spasm of the muscle that is made in the gangrene.
¶ About the method of cauterization in Podagra, and the pain of the joints.
When the pain of the joints is caused by cold humors that are poured on any part of the body, then when the pain occurs in the feet, it is the custom of physicians to call this Podagra properly.
When Podagra is treated with cold causes of pain and the pains do not remain, then the cauterization removes them.
And it is that the cauterization is done on him after evacuation in the circumference of the joints of the feet, with many cauterizations: and the cauterization should be olive oil.
And if you need to make points on the face of the foot, then make with the cauterization points the points. When painful sensations rise up to the knees or other wounds, and this happens frequently, then cauterize the whole knee with three or four cauteries, or from all sides, with the same cauterization as Claudius.
If more is needed of this cauterization, then cauterize it again. And do not dip your hand in the cauterization, rather it is about the thickness of the skin alone.
If painful sensations rise up to the knees and back, then administer what I have said from the cauterization chapter.
If painful sensations are only in the hands, then make punctures around the focus, like the two lines that revolve.
If painful sensations remain in the fingers, then make punctures on all nodes with a single puncture, and on the thumb of the hand.
If painful sensations rise up to the elbows or hips after a day, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not discard the weak one from good management, from the reception of the physician. For if a good regimen is made, and the phlegm is discarded, it will be healed with the help of God by this cauterization.
§ On the method of cauterization in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groins, and the intestine descends, or the gut to the testicle, and this is nearest approaching: then it is necessary to let the weak one discard food on that day. And let him use gentle food, by which the feces may come out from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and make him hold his breath until he goes out, or shows the gut, or the intestine.
Then reduce again your fingers, and the signs with caustic under the rupture on the sides of the eyes, with a sign whose end is similar to half a circle in the upper part of the body.
Then apply the caustic, which is in this form, until it turns white and comes out as flakes. Then reduce the intestine, or the colon to its connexion. Then place his hand over the place so that it does not escape from the intestine: and you have already opened between the weak thighs, and placed under it a pillow, and another on the crura of his other leg, and another on his chest which holds the hand.
Then place the caustic over the sign with your hand holding the cauterium straight. And hold it, until when you reach the mouth: or go with another if you do not succeed with this one up to the mouth.
And observe wisely from the exit of the intestine in the hour of your cauterization, lest you burn it, and may appear by this on the weak or through malice great death.
And know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cauterium, your operation will not be successful.
And it is necessary that the cauterium for children be fine according to their measure.
Then care for the wound with the rest of the ointments until it heals.
And let him be weak lying on his back for forty days, until the wound is scabbed over.
And it is necessary that you place food on his length of time of curing according to the length of his wound healing so that his belly does not escape from the connexion and excretion.
Then when you want to rise after forty days, then administer the bandage made in a proper way, and hold it for forty days with others.
And it may be lessened by labor, and fullness of food and drink, and loud speaking.
For when this regimen is used, it is cured wholly by the cure.
And I say that the treatment of ruptures with incision in its chapter.
When however ruptures happen in the other belly, and they are beginning, and you do not wish them to be added, then cauterize the rupture with a round cauterization of the same quantity: and this which hardens from then on shall be as the third of it. Then take care of it itself, according to what we have said: and it will not be added.
And some have already said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cauterization, according to this form.
After it is set alight with the caustic, and a line is put across it which is along its width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line downwards. And place your hand in the middle with the caustic closed.
But the caustic is first easier and better.
¶ About the method of cauterization in pain due to wound or percussion.
Head 48.
When it happens in some members by wound or percussion of pain: and he has endured the pain for a long time, and it does not consent to the cure with medicines: then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the point caustic.
And the caustic should be a cauterization for all members according to its size, and the parity of it, and its weakness, and its vigor, and its location of twisting, and the pain from it.
If then it is cured by the first cauterization, it is good. If not, then proceed with the same cauterization.
For these pains are of habit, and they ought to be changed from the member towards that which is nearest to it. Therefore it is necessary to seize these pains with cauterization, until the weak one is healed.
¶ On the manner of cauterization in Leprosy.
However, in leprosy sometimes the cauterization is made with the greatest cauterization. And especially the kind of leprosy which is made for putrefaction of the phlegmatic and melancholic: since when you wish to cauterize it, consider it.
If then leprosy is sloughing, and you have treated it with that which we said in the division, and it has not gone down, nor yet: and you fear for the weak one, that corruption may comprehend all the complexion of it: then cauterize it on the head with five burns: one in the middle of the head, and another under it at the end of the hair, and two under the two horns, and one under the nail of the little finger.
And then your hand with cauterization almost, until it makes an impression in the mouth of a small print, and the cortices are dislocated from it: that the breath of the gross vapors may escape from it, and cauterize also on the spleen, according as it precedes.
But if leprosy has already spread over the weak one and appears clearly: then it is necessary to cauterize with those burns which we said in the head, and on the end of the nose, and two on the two maxillae, and two on the two spines of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large on the hips and one above it, in the same hip: and two on the thighs, i.e. one on the whole thigh, and two on the knees, and two on the elbows, and two on the breast-bones of his own: and cauterize it on all the joints, from the joints of the fingers of his hands, and feet: and cauterize on all the heel of his feet, and the nails of his hands.
Because of this, for the nerves that are above the last heel bone, so that they do not burn them.
And when the caustic is applied to the os pectoralis, and another above the os stomachi, and another above the epar.
And you know that the more you add to the caustic, the more inflammation and the more consolidating it becomes.
And you know that the weak do not find pain in the caustic as the healthy do, because their body is already stunned.
And it should be that the caustics are according to their size and thickness, according to the parts and seams: according to what precedes from the types of tools.
Then take care of the caustic from the flour of plants with honey, and the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
¶ On the method of cauterization in Stupor.
When a certain member is stunned and is treated with medicines, oils, plasters, and does not heal, then cauterize the stunned member with caustics according to the size of the member or its thickness.
And your caustic should be transverse in the thickness of the skin, almost. Then take care of it with ointment until it is healed.
And when a certain stupor occurs that happens to the hand and foot, and in the shoulders at the exit of the nerves that move that member: and the stupor is removed.
Indeed, do not assume it for that unless one is wise in the anatomy of the members, and the egress of the nerves that move the body.
Head LIV.
When the ancient Albaras no longer contains anything of medical engineering: then cauterize over the deep cauterization as soon as possible, according to the degree of skin thickness, until the white removes and changes its color.
Then treat it with flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossum, and blood of the pigeon, and blood of the swallow: each part is one: mix all these together and they will stick to the cloth and remain in place until it heals.
¶ On the method of cauterization in cancer.
When cancer is beginning and you want to hold it in place: then cauterize it with the cauterization circle around it, just as it rotates.
But wise men said that it should be cauterized with the last cauterization in the middle.
But I do not see that: for I fear that it will ulcerate, and I have already seen that several times.
And it is better to cauterize around it with a circle as we said, or with many cauterizations.
¶ On the method of cauterization in adhesions.
When someone has adhesions and it is slow to mature, or because of the excessive making of it, or because of the weakness of the old, when there are few drops of blood, or because of time, and you want to hasten the maturation of the adhesions: then cauterize around it with many small cauterizations. Then release it. For it will hasten with the maturation.
If however you want to make a hole in it with the cauterization, then burn this one with the cauterization, whose form is this one.
And place it directly in the middle of the dressing, until it penetrates the skin: and let it be a cauterization from which a weak one follows, so that the course may be cleansed purely.
Then take care of it until it heals.
§ Method of cauterization in corroding matter.
Head LXXXIV. (This is likely a reference to the size or degree of the wound, not a patient's age or name.)
The corroding is only a decay in a walking member, and it corrodes itself, just as fire consumes dry wood.
If then you see a corroding in the place where the cauterization can endure with fire, then much cauterization, small and large closures, according to which is suitable for that place where the decay is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you completely remove the decay, and nothing remains of it deeply.
Then release it for three days, and place over the cauterized spots powdered sulfur with oil, until all escharas are removed, and all decay.
Then take care of it with the unguents that generate flesh.
If then you see that after three days healthy flesh is generated without decay, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cauterization over the remaining parts of the decaying ones.
And the corroding is sometimes treated with sharp medicine. For it rises at the place of the cauterization.
Indeed, the cauterization with fire is more useful than the medicine: and I have already said that the cauterization of it with sharp medicine in division: take then it here when you need it.
§ Method of cauterization in boils and warts.
Chapter 57.
This affliction often occurs in the lower parts of the foot: it is a large, filtered thing that harms the foot.
Indeed, there is a caustic in those parts according to two ways: the caustic with fire, and the caustic with hot water.
However, when it is with fire, it is like a feather made of flame: which is made of iron, according to the quantity that contains it, closed from all sides: and it has a fine edge.
Then place the hot caustic on the closed part. Then roll the hand with the caustic around the closed part, until the caustic reaches the depth of the closed part: and let it remain for three days, until it begins to emit pus. Then apply the plaster with ointment made of finely ground mustard, and salt: and let it be applied over the caustic at night. For it will be eradicated from its roots.
Then take care of the place with the generated skin ointment, until it is healed.
If they do not heal, and many of them occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet: then apply the caustic with hot water to them: and it is like taking a canula from air, or iron, or from a feather: and place it over the closed part, or an althelul. Then draw out a small amount of hot water from the canula: hold your hand, and roll it with the compression of your hand, so that the edge of the canula is imprinted on the depth of the closed part, and it finds warm water to the root, to the depth: and it will wait weakly for a short time after the application of hot water.
Then let it go, for it will be uprooted along with its roots.
Do it one after another until all of them are removed from the body.
Then take care of them after they have been uprooted, with the ointment that generates flesh from the wound.
¶ Method of Cauterization in Tremors.
When a tremor occurs in someone due to cold in the nerve, or due to a fever of the fourth kind, or otherwise: then it is necessary to cauterize it with four cauterizations, or five over the back of the spine, and over all the back, and in the chest of that person, and over the stomach of that person.
For the tremor ceases with the olive oil cauterization, and hastens the health of the illness of cold.
¶ Method of Cauterization for Albathir.
Head 57.
When the foetid Albathir spots that are formed from the corrupt materials of the body are expelled from the body.
Therefore, it is necessary to first cauterize them when they appear, with the olive oil cauterization over all the head spots, with a fine myrtle stick, whose ends are burned with fire. Or if the long root of the Aristolochia is used. Or if the cauterization with the lens is used.
And when they are cauterized for the removal of adenomas, in the beginning of their expulsion according to this method: and they do not increase: and it breaks down the surplus, making them, and they heal from them.
Nevertheless, it should be done after the venesection with bloodletting.
On the method of cauterization in the flow of blood from an artery into the thigh.
It often happens that the flow of blood from an artery, which is incised on the thigh, occurs externally, or at the site of the incision, or at the site of the cauterization of the member, and similar to these, it is difficult to cut it off.
When this happens to someone, then immediately with your hand on the arterial opening, and place your thumb on it: and tighten it much until the blood is pressed under your thumb, and nothing escapes from it.
Then place the small olive-oil cauterization on the fire, and a large number of them, and blow on them until they are burned.
Then take one of them, whether small or large, according to the thigh and the place where the artery is cut, and place the cauterization on the same vein, after which you remove your thumb quickly: and hold the cauterization until the blood is cut off.
If it is expelled with your thumb from the arterial opening, and the cauterization is extinguished, then take another cauterization quickly, from the cauterizations that are prepared in the fire.
So do not stop doing this with one after another, until the blood is cut off.
And be careful not to burn the nerve that is there, and another evil may occur above it.
And you know that when the blood flows out of the artery, it is not possible to cut it off at that time: especially if the artery is large, unless with one-fourth of a drachm. Or if with cauterization, as we have said. If there is no extraction, then there is no extraction. When it is extracted, its ends are contracted, and blood is cut off. Or if it is sewn up with a strong thread. Or let them be applied to it according to the properties of the medicine that cuts off blood and is suitable for a tight constriction.
However, if the administrator cuts off its blood with a ligature, and tightens it with cloth, or with the arrangement of things burning, and similar things, it does not conflict with him severely, except rarely.
If something like that happens to someone, and there is no present physician or medicine, then he should begin with placing the first digit of the index finger on the opening of the wound, as we have said, and a tight constriction, until the blood is squeezed out from the upper part of the wound, and above the artery. And the finger should not be removed, but continue to apply it to the cold water of the freezing ice, until the blood is frozen and hardened, and then cut off.
And in the meantime, he should consider what he needs from the cauterization, or from the medicine.
On Incision, Perforation, and Phlebotomy in wounds, and similar things.
As we have said in Chapter One, all the ailments in which the fire of the cauterization and the medicine burning, and their occasions, causes, the instruments of cauterization, and the forms of cauterization are mentioned.
And I have placed this chapter from the head to the foot.
And I will proceed in this chapter in the same vein: so that it may be raised over the seeker of what is sought.
Before I begin this chapter, it is necessary for you, my sons, to add that there is fear in this chapter concerning cauterization, which is not present in the first chapter on cauterization.
Therefore, caution must be greater in this operation, as often blood comes out with it, which is the cause of fear among the wounds, incisions on the scalp, abscesses, wounds for extracting arrows, curing wounds, and extracting stones, and those similar to them. From all of which there is associated terror and fear, and death occurs in many of them.
I warn you not to let that fall on you, for sometimes men with weaknesses in this art fall on you. For among them is one who is angry with his own sickness and death is near to him because of his great anger, which he finds from his own weakness and the length of his malice. And when sickness comes, it is from fear of death.
And among them is one who gives his servant to you and says to you with him, hoping for your health, and his sickness is dangerous.
Therefore, it does not need to be that you consent to him who comes to you from them, of whose manner it is such. And let our caution be greater than our greed and rapacity. And do not presume over anything from him, unless you have certain knowledge that verifies this to you among the successful succession.
And use your knowledge in the care of all your sick, by prophecy and indication to it that health is conveniently suitable.
In that there is an helper to you in the acquisition of fame and glory, and memory and praise.
May God inspire you, O sons, with His understanding, and He will not take away from you His guidance and inspiration, for it is in His hand.
And I myself have divided this chapter into sections according to the order of the previous chapter on cauterization, from the ear to the feet, so that what you seek from it may be revealed to you and where you need it.
¶ Regarding the treatment of water collected in the skulls of children.
Head I.
Know that this affliction often happens to children during childbirth: or when the mother tightens the head of the child without causing it to bleed.
And whenever it happens due to a hidden cause which is unknown.
And I myself have not seen this affliction in others except in children, and for all of them who came to me before they died, therefore it is fitting for me to interrupt the operation on her.
And I myself have seen a child whose head was filled with water, and his head became magnificent throughout the day, until he could not sit on himself because of the magnitude of his head, and the moisture increased until he died.
And this moisture indeed collects between the skin and the face, or it collects above the bones on the side of the face.
And the operation on him, if there is moisture between the skin and the face, and the edema is small, then it is necessary to make a cut in the middle of the scalp in a horizontal direction: and the length of the fissure should be like two knots, until the moisture flows.
And this is a spumous shape.
If then the moisture is more increased, and the edema is greater, then place them two fissures according to this shape.
If moisture is under the bone, and its sign is that which you see open wounds of the head from all sides: and water is removed when you compress it with your hand to the inside, and it does not hide from you this: then it is necessary for you to find in the middle of the head three fissures, according to this manner.
And after making the incision, remove all the moisture outside. Then string the fissures with pieces of cloth and silk. Then apply this with wine and oil up to the fifth day.
Then dissolve the ligament, and care for the wound with bandages, and ointments.
And do not let go of tying the head with equality. And drink a little moist food, until the member is strengthened and healed.
And another mode of incision is, according to which you will see the magnitude of the posters and the collection of water.
For sometimes it is in the back, or in the heel, or on the right side, or on the left side.
Therefore, ascend with the incision where you see the posters and the collection of water, and divide it according to what you can.
And observe, do not rupture the artery, and let there be a flow of blood, and the weak one dies from that flow with the flow of moisture.
¶ About the incision of the arteries that are behind the ears.
Head 2.
When there occurs to someone cataract to the eyes, or to the chest, and it becomes old and does not help the treatment of physicians: then the last treatment is in this, the incision of these two arteries.
Therefore, when you want to incise them, let the weak head of your own radiate. Then scrape the area with a rough cloth so the arteries appear. Then he weakly stretches his neck with any cloth of his own. Then consider where the pulse of the vein is. And the location of both is that which is behind the ears depressed: and it is rarely hidden, unless in some few people.
Then signs are made with wax over both: and cut through both with a sharp knife, incision being applied to the bone, and make it go around the circumference of the head.
And if you wish, insert the knife under the artery, and cut it to the upper part with the incision.
And the length of the incision should be roughly two fingers joined.
For when the vein is cut, blood will flow out of the pulse-like ejection, which frequently jumps to the inside.
However, if the artery does not appear by touch, then it is necessary to measure the distance from the ear with a space of three fingers. Then signs are made with wax, and find until the bone.
And that which should be expelled from the blood is six grains, and perhaps you will expel more or less. All of this according to the amount that appears to you from the weak vein and the fullness of the artery of it.
Then consider to the thigh. Then if there remains something to the bone from the incision, then cut it so as not to cause a hot burn: then tie the thigh with threads from linen cloth.
Then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
¶ About the extraction of arteries that are in time.
¶ Head 3.
When a man suffers from an old hemicrane, or an acute cataract due to the sharpness of sharp substances, and the heat in the fingers of the thumbs, or soda old, bitter, and similar to these: and is treated with the methods of medical treatment, and it does not agree with this: then we have learned in these diseases the extraction of arteries from the thumbs, or cauterization of these, as we have mentioned.
And the method of the operation in the extraction of these is that it unravels the weak hairs that are in the thumbs, and directs to the apparent artery in the thumb. Indeed, it is shown to you from its own pulse, and is rarely hidden unless in a few men, or excessive coldness.
If it is hidden from you, then it tightly grasps its own weak head with any of its own cloth: then it rubs the place with a rough cloth. Or it may rub the place with hot water until it appears to you with a clear appearance. Then take a sponge, which we formed slightly before. Then it scrubs the skin with it, with ease, until the pustules reach the artery. Then remove the wart with it, and pull it out to the upper part, until you pull it out from the skin, and make it come out of all the cloths that are under it.
If the artery is thin: then cover it with the end of the wart. Then cut off from it a piece according to the quantity by which its ends extend and contract, and there is no flow of blood. For if it is not cut off, and if it is not cut off, the blood does not rise greatly.
Then take out the blood from the vein of the patient, up to three ounces.
If the artery is large, then it should be tied in two places with threads twice as thick and strong as serice, or from the alopecia chord, so that it does not reach putrefaction before the consolidation of the wound, and a flow of blood occurs.
Then cut over the excess between the two ties. Do this at that hour, or at another hour later.
And if you wish, cauterize it with cauterization up to the mouth, with a kitchen cauterization tool: until the ends of its extremities, and it will stay in the same place of the operation.
And it is better to do this unless the patient has a fever or cold complexion. For cauterization is from those that dry out wet things. Therefore it is better to dry them.
And it is necessary after the extraction of the artery to fill the old cloth place: and they should be placed above on the same pillows made.
And after the solution is given with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with linen, until it heals.
If in the meantime while you are operating a flow of blood from the artery, then cut it off with cauterization, or until it fills the place with zegi: and tighten your hand until the blood is cut off. If nothing of these is present to you, then place your thumb above the place until the blood freezes. And rub the place with cold water until the sharpness is quiet and tightens according to what is necessary.
And since that which is leucine and easier for the extraction of the artery is, to cauterize it with this cauterization tool having two kitchen knives: and the sharpness of the two knives should be similar to the magnetite. Indeed, they are much less sharp than two awls. For if they are sharp like two awls, then both coldness will follow: and they do not cause the flesh to be wounded. When there is a little grossness in them, the heat of fire is held by them, and the flesh is wounded carelessly: and therefore this work is better than all others, and more useful, and easier.
And this is the form of cauterization.
And let there be a space between two awls, the quantity of grossness of the fingers, after you have marked out two places with the encaustic: and lay them aside until they become hot to the mouth, and they will happen in two places: so that it may be elongated which is between the extremities of it. For they do not become firm with this cauterization deeply.
Head IV.
Regarding the care of the course of sharp, frequent lachrymal drops from the eyes.
When the tears are frequent and the course of them from the nose which is above the outside of the forehead of the head: and it does not fit anything of the care of medicine with other medicines, and you see the face of the weak one to be reddening, and he feels in his front a walk, as it is the walk of ants: and his eyes are drooping, moist, so that his hairs are already corroded by the corrosion: and his eyelids are hot from the sharpness of the tears: then the ancients used this care for this operation, and called it the care, with Ense.
And it is as you say, to make the weak one's hairs to be corroded which are in his front. Then make three incisions in the front, equally distant according to the length of the face: and let the length of the incision be almost two fingers, and the second one should be in the middle of the nose in the front, and the third according to the length almost as much as the movement of the thumb, and the third from the other side: and take care not to cut any arteries which are in the two sides: and elongate your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let there be a space of all the quantity of three fingers connected: and let there be for you a sponge cut in a frustum, or many dry cloths with which you will dry the blood.
Then insert the sharp end of a sponge of two kinds, whose next form is as follows: After the incision made on the side of the temporal bone, until the second incision: and it will exfoliate the entire skin that is between the two incisions, when you smear with what is above the eye. Then do this also from the middle incision to the second one. Then remove this sharp sponge, and insert the other instrument into the first incision again, which is called the lancet, from one part gently, not sharply from the other part. And this is its form.
And place the sharp side of its flank against the exposed flesh with the skin, and the other side gently against the eye: and push it until it reaches the middle incision: and cut away all the moisture that comes down from the hair to the eyes, except for what is continuous with the incision up to the one that appears from the skin.
Then do this in the middle fissure until the other fissure.
And after it runs out of blood, express the equal quantity of coagulated blood from the points of the splinters.
Then place linen strips in all the fissures, and put on top of them absorbent wool soaked in wine, or oil, or vinegar. And see if a hot blister does not occur.
And on the third day dissolve the bandage, and give a large infusion with warm water. Then care for it with the basilic ointment, and the rest of the ointments used to heal it, until it is cured.
Chapter 5
¶ About the care of sharp lachrymal and catarrhal discharge to the eyes from the inner part of the head.
When a sharp cataract occurs, it is often and persistently attended by small, weak eyes, pale aspect, ulcerated eyelids, falling lashes, deep pain in the head, distressing, and followed by sneezing: then take from these symptoms the one that does not come from the matter of the cataract, unless it comes from many wives.
And this is a better remedy for them. And it is best to have the patient shave his face. Then make a single incision in the middle of his forehead, or another perhaps further to the side, and start from the left temple to the right temple, making the cut until you reach the nose: then extend your hand from the wrists that are biting during mastication, until the nose is caught, and dry all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate the two incisions between the two old lips, or with linen threads. Then sew them up from above with small thread: and moisten the threads with wine and oil, so as not to cause an inflammation of the wound.
And when you have uncovered it, and see that inflammation is about to occur: then it is necessary to cauterize the nose, until flesh begins to be born in it.
Then care for it with the regimen of exiccatus that makes flesh be born, as if you took two parts from the flour of wheat, and four parts from collophonia, and prepare an ointment from them, and apply it to the birth of the flesh in these wounds.
Chapter Six.
¶ About the cure that falls into Aurem.
All that falls on the eye is of four kinds: either a mineral stone, or one similar to stone, such as iron and copper; or it is of plant origin, such as chestnut and sesame; or it is a flowable substance, such as water, vinegar, and their likes; or some animal.
When a stone falls on the eye, or a kind of stone not added to it, and does not grow in gold, expose the gold alone: if you see a stone, then distill something from olive oil or pitch into the gold. Then administer the extraction of it, and make it stir with a condiment, and stuff the nose with the coming sternutation, after you have placed in the circumference of the ear some fragments from the net or cloth, and extended the ear to the upper parts.
For this treatment often goes out.
If it does not go out, then administer the extraction of it with the Gest, that is, Pizigarolis subtle: whose form is this.
If it goes out with the Gest, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction of it with a little bit of the blind's honey subtle, repeated several times.
If it does not go out by this, then make a tube of silver, and insert the end of the tube into the opening of the ear very much, and stuff what is in the circumference of the tube with softened oil with a cork, so that it does not drip but from the tube: then draw it out with your strong attraction.
For this often goes out that we have told. If it does not go out in this way, then take from the helkebat, or from the grain, that is, the prepared flour, with which they take the seeds, a small piece: and put it at the end of the radius after you have placed on it the proper seat: then insert it into the opening of the ear with ease, after you have dried the ear from the moisture.
If then he does not depart with all those which I have mentioned, then immediately towards the cutting, before the heat of the post comes on, or spasm.
And the mode of incision is such that the weak phlebitome is first taken from the head: and then draw it out from the blood according to its strength. Then make the weak one sit down between your hands, and turn his ear upwards, and find a small incision at the root of the ear near the fatty part of the lobe in the depressing place on his own: and let the incision be in the shape of the moon, until it is covered over by the stone: then take it away with it, which is possible for you from your instruments.
Then make the incision with your sharp knife, and take care of it until it is healed.
If the falling in the ear is from one large grain which grows and swells: then give him the extraction of that.
If he does not obey you to the end: then take a thin sponge, fine and of this shape.
And give it with it the abscission of that kind from the grains which fall in the ear, and do not make this when you think that the grain is already moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you put it on many chips: then take it away with tweezers, or with a gentle touch, or with suction as I have said, for the extraction of his abscess is watery.
But if water is entering into the ear, it is necessary that the weak one uses his sternutation with the condyle at first: and he has filled his own ear with some old cotton: and he is lying on that ear which has the water. If then he departs through that, it is good.
If not: then take many stones, according to the length of the finger, thin ones, lenitive, and heat them with fire rather briefly, and insert one of the weaker ones into the ear of that same animal: and let it bite on one of its feet, and strike with a stone other than that stone upon the stone which is in the ear. Therefore, he would not cease doing this with stones and stones, until the entire water has flowed out.
And the water has already flowed out, so take one from parpyro, or from the jaw, and insert the end of it into the ear: and light the other end with fire until it burns the most of it. Then take another jaw, and do this many times, until the entire water has flowed out: and pull out the same one with the cannula according to what was said earlier in the stone.
In the extraction of the animal that was inserted into it, if it is a small body, like a flea, and another similar one, take care of it as I said in the division.
But if it is a large body that appears to the senses: then administer the extraction of its with your hand, and stitches: and this is easier for all that are held in the ear.
In the extraction of the ears generated in the ear, when you care for it with what I said in the division, and in the treatment of distillations, and not your care is intertwined: then it is necessary to look at the ear in the sun. If therefore something appears to you from the ears: then pull it out with your hand, or with fine stitches.
If however something does not appear to you from the ears: then take the cannula whose form is this, with a strict lower part and a wide upper part: and insert the subtle end of it into the ear according to the quantity that the weak one can bear: and then suck with it a strong suction. Perform this many times until all worms come out.
However, if they do not obey you to the end, then wrap the cannula around the plug as I said on the stone.
If they do not come out with what I said: then administer the distillations that the ancients have already tried for the expulsion of worms: and you will find this in the book on distillations.
And may your flow be like when I pour olive oil and medicines into the ear with this instrument whose form is depicted here. As you see, make it like you see it, either of silver or air, lower and tighter, in which there is a small hole above.
It should be that what is in the connection of the cannula, be made of silver. And if you will, take the radium, and wrap the end of the cotton around it in a suitable way: then press out the oil, or grease, or whatever you want from these medicines into the cannula, and it should be in the ear: then insert the radium with the cotton wrapped around it, and expel it with your compressed but gentle hand until the oil is pushed through the connection heard, and feels weak inside: and that which is poured into the ear should be already hot with fire almost: and be careful not to put something cold in it, because medicines do not tolerate that.
Chapter VII.
¶ About the care of the occurrences of silvering.
Sometimes certain infants come out of the wombs of their mothers unperforated.
And it also happens to some people, poverty in the ear of the ear, or flesh born in it.
And this poverty sometimes happens in a deep hole of the ear, which does not follow habit: and sometimes it happens to the outer opening, and follows it.
That which happens in the deep ear, and which is not comprehended by sight, is difficult to treat in many ways.
And in that which follows, use the weak ear in the sun, and look at it: then if you see an apparent opacification, open it with a soft soap of this kind, whose form is as follows: its extremity is where there is some small latitude, whose acute part is a part of it; and the rest of the soap is of two soft sides: so that it will not hurt the ear.
If the opacification is from flesh in the ear: then hold it with a thin shave, and cut it with ease of the strong one, until all the flesh is removed.
If the opacification is in the deep ear: then take a thin, soft heating substance, and heat it slightly: then insert it into the ear.
If you feel an opacification with that which the weak one finds with age in hearing, try to open it with ease: and be careful not to wound the nerves of the ear.
Then place the linen according to the size of the hole you have made in the Egyptian ointment: do this for a few days until you are sure about the healing of the wound.
Or take the linen and pour it into hot water, and rub the ground alum on top of it, and use it yourself.
If you see the ear already swelling: then it is necessary to take out the linen and let it be with another linen that has been soaked in ointment made with hot wax, until the swelling is hot: then care for it until it heals.
If blood flow occurs: then submerge a sponge, or pieces of cloth in cold water, and place your ear over it: and use the remaining treatment, which the aforementioned book of distillations advises for closing the said blood flow.
¶ On the care of Althelia's eyes.
Chapter VIII.
These Altheli that occur in the eyes, sometimes they are moist and sometimes they are dry.
Therefore it is necessary to hold them with tweezers, or with a nail, and to scrape them off with soap from their roots. Then place it on the shaved areas.
If then blood flows from them, then cauterize them with a fine-pointed cauterizing iron.
And cauterizing them is better after the incision. For many of them return when there remains something from their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots burn and do not return.
¶ On the care of Grandin's eyes.
Chapter IX.
Many things happen in the eyes that resemble Grandin in his strength, and in his hardness, and for that reason it is called Grando: it is an aggregation of thick moisture on the upper eyelid, and on the lower eyelid.
Therefore the operation on them is that you consider now, if it is Grando proceeding from it, which appears on the eyelid, and they are moved to all parts, and its matter is easy.
Therefore find a slit on it across its width. Then exfoliate it from all sides with ease until it oozes. Then suspend it with a nail, and cauterize it.
If, however, the abscess is not prepared for you beforehand, unless you penetrate the eyelid with the incision almost immediately after it, it will harm that patient in some way.
If the incision is large: then gather that with the suture: and take care of it until it heals.
And if it is small, it will not harm you from it. A ointment, however, will restore it and make it supple.
And if the grain is turned towards the inner part of the ear, and passes through the intrinsic surface of the eyelid, then the eyelid, and suspend the grain with a gilded needle: besides which you need an incision, and press it from all sides.
If the eyelid is extended by the incision, it will not harm anything.
Then wash the eye after the gilded grain incision with salt water: and take care of the place where it becomes supple, until the weak one is healed.
¶ About the care of Axinath's eyelids.
Chapter X.
Axinath is a wax that is generated in the upper eyelids' furs: and it happens most of all to children: and it grieves their eyes, and cataracts happen to them in the morning, and they cannot see the sun's light, because the tears are directed towards them, and for this reason they should lie down on their faces at all times, and sleep on them, and their eyelids are always wet, because the inflation has already occurred: and the apparent size of Axinath is indeed in the eye, and when you take the place with your fingers, you feel Axinath between them.

Then find in the middle of its moisture with sandpaper, when it is incident, cracks through the breadth, and there should not be a crack larger than that which is made in phlebotomy in the deep.
Or it may be that you find the entire skin, until the inflammation reaches Axrinath, because many times Axrinath comes out of the fissure according to the shape of white wool.
Then take it out with the cloth that you have inserted between your fingers to the outside: and turn your hand to the right and left until it is swept away: and be careful not to add in the crack so that there is no inflammation with sandpaper to the eye, and hurt it.
However, if Axrinath does not appear to you at the beginning of the crack, add a little with ease in the crack until Axrinath comes out. Then take it out as I said.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the place, and tie it with threads.
And from men there are those who pour salt on the crack, and place it in the liquid that remains from that moisture.
Then take care of it until it is healed.

Head XII.
§ About the burning of the hairs that prick in the eye with a needle.
The operation in this is, to take a fine thread, and to thrust it into it with a fine needle, gently. Then gather the extremities thereof, and the nodes of both knots with fine needles: and the length of the threads shall be a thumb's breadth.
Then compose another fine thread under it, and if you will, the extremities of those threads.
Then lay his weak head near the sun, and it shall be near the earth, because it is a subtle or small operation.
Then thrust the needle with the threads into the root of the eyelid, and make it pierce the eyelid quickly, until it comes out above the natural hair.
Then draw the thread up to the knots: and thrust the thread into the knots: if it be one, or two, or three, not more.
Then draw your hand with it, until the hair with the knots comes out with the natural hair of the eyelid.
If then the knots are drawn out, and the hair does not come out with them: draw the knots towards the lower part, with the thread which you have composed in it, until the knot comes out of the upper opening, and see it by the eye: then draw the knot and the thread: and take out both, and close the eye: and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place, and the flesh is born over it.
If the hair is short, then associate it with a long hair from natural hair, and pluck it while holding it. Or release it until it stretches after some time, and then pluck it then.

Chapter XVIII.

When you have completed your application, then distill it into the eye of the green ivory, or red: so that its own sharpness may consume what remains of the original.

When the eye is prominent with all its bulk, and there is no hurt in use, nor diminution: then it is necessary to loosen the weak one: then draw out the blood: afterwards put on wet dressings without scarification, but with suction.
Then place a liniment made from acacia, aloe, frankincense, and sarsaparilla over the eye. Then pull down the eyelid over the plaster with many pins.
And the mode of the pins is: take many thin linen cloths, and double each one four times, then use as many as you wish from them on the eye, then place them one over the other according to the size of the eye, and then tighten them with a strong bandage.
And repeat the incisions without scarring with wet gauze.
Then remove the incisions and let the eyelid tightened for one day and night.
However, if the bandage is again softened, then it should be tightened greatly: then remove the bandage as we have said.
If then you see the eye already red with a soft bandage, it is good: and if not, then repeat the plaster, the pins, the tightening, and the incisions until it heals.
§ On the incision of the eye covering.
Head 21.
When a rupture occurs in the eye covering, then it should be cut off and comes out of the eyelid as a grain of wheat, and disfigures the appearance of man because of this, and it is supposed to be sewn in: then the operation is done in this way, according to what I will describe: and it is, that you thrust an acorn into the root of the wheat from the lower part to the upper part.
Then thrust another acorn into the part where there is a thread that is double the size of the tear duct, and make it penetrate: and remove the first according to its position.
Then cut out the part where there is a thread that is double the size of the wheat, and sew it to the part of the wheat around the acorn, and tighten it greatly.
Then extract the eye socket and place a sponge soaked in warm water on top of it, then release it until the thread falls with the king.
Then care for the eye with it, so that it strengthens it until it heals.
And when it is tightened by the king around all parts with a circle on cloth, until it adds the eye a great prominence.
Then it is polished with fine sandpaper, which reaches deep into the eye, and moistens the albino, and the eye goes down and enters immediately: then tighten it, until it heals.
¶ Regarding the treatment of Alcomnati.

Chapter 24.
About the care of the flesh of the newborn in the nose.

Chapter 30.
¶ About the extraction of tooth pain.
It is necessary that you cure the tooth from its pain with all ingenuity, and then in its excision. We have already seen this from the operation of bloodletting.
When the tooth itself is certified as painful to you, then it is necessary to scarify around the tooth with soot, in which there is some virtue, until the gum is loosened from all sides: then move it with your fingers or with the smallest pincers at first gently, until you stir it up.
Then place the large forceps good and firmly in that place, and the weak head between your thighs: which you have held well, so that it does not move: then pull the tooth according to its right direction, so as not to break it.
If it does not come out, then take one of their instruments and introduce it under it from all sides with ease, and stir up its motion, as you have done at first.
But if the tooth is perforated or corroded, then it is necessary to fill that hole with a piece of cloth: and tie it up with the fine ends of the ribbons, so that it does not break in the tightening of your forceps over it.
And you should be very careful with the scarring around the gum from all sides.
And watch your strength, so as not to break it, and there remains a part of it, and returns to the weakness of that malice which is the greater pain of its first.

Many times they cause great injuries to the bodies of men, whose wounds are the most difficult to heal, and all the roots of which remain, or some of them: or such as remove it with some of the bones of the jaw: as we have often testified.
Then follow the application of wine after its removal, or with vinegar and salt.
If blood flows from the wounds (for it often happens), then mix something from the zegi with the blood, and fill that place: and if not, cauterize the wound so that the zegi does not harm you.
The forms of the sharp-pointed hooves by which the tooth moves should be long at both ends, short in the middle, thick, so that they do not double when they press on the tooth: they should be like the hooves of oxen, until when you tighten them with them, they do not bend towards themselves, nor double: thin at both ends, and they should be made of iron or of the nail, or of such as are fit for the ends: and in their ends there should be teeth, some of which go into some, and tighten by a suitable constriction.
And sometimes they become like the end of the jaw of a bird called the cuckoo, and are strong in constriction.
