Head 32.
Regarding the cutting of prominent teeth above others.
When teeth are prominent and do not follow their natural course, a monstrous form is formed: and especially when this happens in women and girls, that is, virgins.
Therefore, you should consider this. For if the tooth is born after another tooth and is not placed or its cutting is possible, or its filing, then remove it: and if it is connected with another tooth, then cut it off with this instrument, which is of this form.
This is a small face, and it is made from iron with sharp pointed ends.
And your cutting should be such that you cut into many days, and because of the hardness of the teeth, and so as not to disturb another tooth.
However, if the tooth is prominently exposed to its filing, then file it with a file of this form.
The whole should be of iron, and the handle of the punch should be as small as the point of the spicules, with which the tooth is filed gradually over many days with ease, so as not to disturb the tooth, and fall off: then smooth it down, and finally scrape it off with some rasps.
If the tooth from which a part breaks off and harms the tongue is, then it should be filed so that its filing also removes the roughness of that fragment, and makes it even: and it will flatten and not hurt the tongue, nor corrupt the speech.
Chapter 33.
On the representation of the tooth with golden sons.
When an injury occurs to the anterior teeth due to a blow or accident, and the weak cannot hold onto it to prevent it from falling: and they are cared for with stimulant medicines, and the cure is not avoided: then the wisdom is that they should be fastened with a golden wire: because silver becomes shiny and rots after days, but gold never changes.
And the wire should be of medium thickness and size according to the amount that can be held between the teeth.
And the form of the representation is to take the wire, and insert it twice between two healthy teeth: then you should twist with two ends of the wire between the moving teeth, whether one or more, until inflammation with a cloth up to the other part of the sound tooth. Then repeat the twisting up to the part where you fell: and hold your hand with subtlety and wisdom, until it is not removed at all: and your binding should be such that when you fasten the wire at the roots of the teeth, it will not fall apart.
Then cut off the excess ends of the wire with a knife: and gather them up, and turn them together with your hand: and hide them between the sound tooth and the moving tooth, so that they do not hurt the tongue: and then let it remain tight as long as it remains.
But if it is loosened or falls off, fasten them with another wire, and let it remain tight for the whole time.
And this is the form of the tooth, and the representation of the two sound teeth and the two moving teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that one tooth comes out, or two after a blow or accident in its place, and remains as we have described, and remains: and this is done only by the craftsman, wise, and experienced.
When the bone spur once fits into the joint: it takes the form of a tooth and is placed in its place, from which the tooth is fastened and drawn tight, as I have said: and it remains, and serves for a long time.
Chapter XLII.
When the ligament that occurs under the tongue is either natural, as it is when man is born, or accidental, from the bone that has already solidified.

Cure of two breasts.
Chapter 36.
Whenever two breasts occur in the throat, that is, glands that resemble cotton, which occur in the deformed: and they are called two Amigdalae: when you care for them with what I said in division and they do not heal, then consider.

If it is of a white color, round, and its root is fine: then it should be cut.
And the operation should be made in it, as you consider before its own operation, if the hot aposteme is quietly completed, or if it is about to diminish by some reduction: then let the weak one sit before the sun, and the head of it should be in your groove: and open its mouth, and take it with your hands, and cut its tongue downwards with the instrument whose form this is.
Let it be made of silver or air, which is as fine as a dagger.

Then cut it with the instrument whose form follows this one. It will resemble thorns: but the ends of them are sharp, so that the orifice of each of them is in the direct acute angle of the other: therefore take care that it is made of iron, or alfuled which drinks up.

When certain stones are born in the throat, other than the two amber ones. Therefore, it should be cut according to what I said about the incision of two amber ones equally.
And I indeed had already treated a woman who had given birth to a stone between the gullet that was drawn towards the throat, which was nearly closed by the gullet: and the woman was breathing through a narrow opening, and had forbidden him food and drink: and she had almost reached death, if it had lasted one day, or two days.

Then I made that which came out of the other nostril opening.

And be careful not to do this treatment at the beginning of the attack with abscesses. For plasters are added to the abscess, and it is not appropriate to do this unless you are at the decline of the hot abscess.
If this instrument is not present to you, then take the vinegar and put the end of the bark in it: so that the weak tooth may not be burned: for the bark of the oui prevents the vapour from burning the tooth: and this is good for the cure of health.
¶ About the extraction of thorns and bones from the mouth.
Head 38.
Many things stick in the throat, either a fish bone, or something else.
Therefore, it should be removed that which appears on it over which it falls, after having placed the tongue with the instrument at the sun, and it will be declared to you what is in the throat.
And what does not appear to you and is hidden in the throat, it is necessary to make a human being before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps the thing attached by vomiting will escape.
Or perhaps the weak one swallows the dry piece of the root, or the root of the lettuce, or swallows a small piece of dry bread: or takes a dry piece of marine seaweed soft, and then ties it in a thread and swallows it. When therefore it becomes wet at the place where the bones or the teeth are, and it is withdrawn, then it will go out.
If it does not go out with that which I said, then use the instrument from the second leg according to this form.
It should be larger than the radius but with a slight curve at its end, so that it can easily insert into its own throat with facility, and it should have its own head elevated upward.
And let it be careful of its own epiglottis so that it does not happen to it a fit, and it pushes with it the tongue or the bone or inserts it itself with its own hand.
Indeed, if the weak one inserts it, this is better: because of its knowledge of the location of the thing attached: and it pushes down or pulls up with its own hand using the instrument, all of it according to the quantity that is prepared for it until it goes out.
¶ About the extraction of bloodletting.
Chapter XXXIX.
When treating a blood-letting wound with the remedy I mentioned during division and not curing it, consider its effects on the weakened mouth before the sun, whether at noon or after speaking its language with the instrument I will show you.
If your habit falls upon the blood-letting wound, remove it with a small beard, or with a gentle gesture.
If that is not possible with them: then take a cannula with a sharp point, and insert it into the weakened throat as far as the throat: then insert a heated iron into the cannula's opening. Do this often: and let the weakened one avoid water all day long.
Then let them drink a full glass of cold water, and open their mouth into it: and wash their mouth with it, and do not swallow anything from it: and repeat this process once an hour after another with their own hand. For the blood-letting wound will fall when it tastes the water.
If it does not follow what we have described, then smoke the weakened one with incense, or with ashes using the instrument I will show you in smoking.
Do this often, for it will fall.
And the method of operation in smoking is to take a pot, in which the old woman's prunes are with fire: and the pot should be covered with a cover, in whose middle there is a hole: and the end of the instrument is placed in that hole.
Then let them blow the smoke, and have the weakened one open their mouth at the end of the cannula, and close it so that it does not fall out of the smoking until you know that the smoking has already reached the blood-letting wound. The bloodletting immediately yields.
If it does not yield, then repeat the fumigation many times.
And the weak one endures the thirst, and eats salt, and honey, and does not drink water.
Therefore, it is necessary to go out with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which bloodletting is taken out of the stomach, when it yields above the used one.
It is like claws, as you see: unless because this thirst which is inserted into the throat. And the end of it is similar to the beak of the owl, which is called the "gallinago," in which there is rough fingers: when it grasps something, it does not let it go at all.
¶ About the opening of the Aposteme, and their section, and care in general.
Chapter 40.
The species of the Aposteme are many, of various kinds, according to which rememoration they come, that is, one and one in this book: and they are diverse in their perforation and section of them from two ways.
One of them is of the kind of Aposteme itself, and that which comprehends from moisture.
And the second mode is for the places where it happens to the body.
For the Aposteme that happens in the head is another from the Aposteme that happens in the anus: and the Aposteme that happens in a fleshy place is another from the Aposteme that happens in joints: and each of them is judged according to its operation.
And from the Aposteme there are those which it is not fit that they should be perforated, unless after the maturation of the sore in them, and the complement of it: and from them there are those which it is necessary that they should be perforated, while they are raw, and do not mature according to the complement.
As the appointed ones who are nearby with joints.
Because when an appointed one happens near the joint, and it is prolonged to be there, until it putrefies that which is in its surrounding, perhaps the ligaments or nerves of his joint are corrupted, therefore the cause of the contraction of his member.
Or is the appointed one at the main member: for if you delay the piercing of it, until it is ripe, it will hurt either him or through that principal member.
Or is near another, therefore the member itself is not ripe: and it is not fitting that you pierce a putrefied one, not fully digested, unless it is near another, so that it does not putrefy deep, and extends to the inner parts of it, and a fistula is made, or in the end of it, which is not cured.
It is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the appointed one, which is ripe according to the complement: and it is near sedation of the pain, recession of the fever, and diminution of the rubedness, and pulsation of the head apostema, and the rest of the signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same piercing in the lower part of the appointed one, and more prominent eminence: and the piercing should be wanding in the length of the body, if the appointed ones are in parts of hands and feet, and of fingers, and of strings, and of strings, and of nerves, and of arteries, and at the last in all equal places where there is no reflexion.
In those that reflect, wand with the piercing according to that member.
When the appointed one is in flesh: then it is better that you let pass the piercing of it, until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said according to the complement.
Since you pierce it before that, the course will be prolonged for a long time from it, and there will be many fouls and bitterness, and perhaps its lips will become hardened, and its depth.
And some piercings are made according to the body's breadth at the time of need: or according to that which the member requires.
It is necessary to make the piercings in the pubic region with a small perforation, and in the larger ones with a large perforation: or make many sections according to the size of the piercing.
And they are from the piercings where it is necessary to cut the skin: and it is applied when the skin is already like a cloth, and it is applied at the end when it is already dead: just as that which happens in many cases, such as the nipples, and the bubons.
And from them there are those that are cut with a section having three angles. And from them there is one, according to which it is applied like the figure of the myrtle leaf.
Just as the pubic piercings.
And from them there are those in which a round section and a lunar section are applied: and similar ones are made from these sections.
However, if it does not have a head, like the surface piercings, it is necessary to pierce it with a superficial perforation, or only flat.
And it is necessary when the piercing is large, and it has already collected a lot of healthy tissue, and it pierces it, so that not too much pus is taken out at once: in fact, take out that part of it. Then fill the piercing up to another day. Then take out some pus again.
Perform this frequently according to the gradation, until it goes out: especially if the person is weak in bodily strength, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an old man with decrepit bones: for the animal spirit, being resolved from one animal to another on going out through the sore, may perhaps cause the death of the weak one, and you may not perceive it.
Therefore, this chapter requires great caution.
And then, after your perforation, which you made with the apostemata for this purpose, it is necessary to cleanse the wound: and consider. If then the wound is small from the apostemata, or if it is a flat section, then apply a linen bandage, or an old hat. And if the wound is large, and there are many perforations, then it is necessary to insert a bandage into all the fissures until they become moist.
And if in the wound you have cut away a part of the skin, or have cauterized it around: then it is necessary to fill it with an old hat, or as when the cloth is tied, or when the hair of linen is combed without moisture: and tie it up until the third day.
Then take it out, and care for it with the ointment, until it is cured.
But if blood flows in your operation, then apply cold water and vinegar, after the cloth has absorbed it: and place it over the place where the blood flow is great.
But if the flow of blood persists, then it is necessary to give a regimen and treatment, and plasters, which I have mentioned in many places of this our books, and by division.
But if it is in the winter season, and the wound is of many nerves: then it is necessary to apply plasters with wine, and hot oil: and place them over the places.
If it is summer and the area is fleshy: then you should put poultices made with water and oil, or wine and oil, and all of this should be cold. When the third day comes, as we have said, then you should dissolve the style, cleanse it, and administer to its treatment what is suitable for it until it recovers.
This is therefore what is necessary from the knowledge of the surgery of the style generally.

Head 41.

Styles that happen on the scalp are small and come from the species of Nodulus, which are found in the clothes made of these shells, which are like the husks of grapes.
And their species is many.
Among them are fat ones: and among them are those that contain like moisture as of the limbs: and among them are those that contain like the moisture of flints and pellitory: and such as these, and among them are those that are hard like stones.
And in the whole section, and there is no fear of its extraction, while it does not cause any contrariety in the artery at its own section.
And the operation in their section is as you will find it with the instrument which comes after this, called the Intromissive, until you know what it contains.
For if it is that which contains moisture, then you should dry it in the section according to the length of the surface section, in this form.
And begin with the section from line b to line g. And when the moisture is evacuated, then you scrape off the chalk which contains that moisture, and do not let anything pass through it.
Many times it returns, if something remains from it.
Then immerse the stomach in Egyptian ointment, if it is present: and if not, in water and salt: and fill the belly with it, and let it go until the next day. For it will itself corrode that remains from the box.
Then go over the stomach with Egyptian ointment a second and third time, and if you need it, until you trust that nothing will remain from the box, then care for the belly with the ointment until it is healed.
If the aposteme contains a red node, then cut it according to this form, with a cross-shaped section: and pull out the hairs between the two sections of the section, and rub it all over: and trust in your virtue in extracting the tunic that contains it.
If the artery causes you contrariness, then do what I will tell you after.
And similarly, do in the aposteme if it is of stone, according to the section and care that I mentioned earlier.
And the section over the stone aposteme is easier: because it is few in blood and moisture. And sometimes there are some of these aposteme in the head of certain men, where there is no moisture at all.
That is: because I followed over the aposteme in the head of a young woman, and found an aposteme like a hard, solid, rough, white stone, which could not be broken: and if it is pricked with anything while being pulled out, it wounds itself.
In others however, accidents in the head of the aposteme, except for these aposteme that happen in the heads of children, and among the roots of gold, the section of all of them is a superficial section.
Either cut off their nails from below, always from the lower part of their nails, so that the course of the sanies might flow downwards.
Then attend to it with caution, as it may harm them in their treatment.
§ Section on the Stripped Throat in the Neck.
Chapter 42.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes in other parts of the body.
And those that occur above them in the neck are few, and many; they are caused by the cold: and every Strophula of them is within the patient's own clothing, just as is the case with nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have said.
And the species of these abscesses are many. For they are made up of stone: and some of them are dry: and some of them are malignant, and do not obey treatment.
In that which appears to be a good abscess in the skin, of which the color of the skin is manifestly close to it, and moves over all parts, and is not annexed to the neck muscles, nor to the jaw, nor to the artery, nor is deep: it is necessary to cut it out superficially from the upper part down to the lower part of the body, along line b. to line g., and scrape it off from all parts: and extend two lips of the skin with the beard, or with many beards, if you desire that, as we said in the abscesses of the head, and draw it out a little at a time.
And it is over the cauterant, so that it does not come into contact with the mind, or the nerve.
And it should be rough but not sharp: so that it does not add to your hand when you make the incision, or disturb the weak, and you cut where you do not need to.
If you happen to injure a vein, an artery, or prevent yourself from performing the operation, then place the cut end of a piece of reed in the vulna, or some children who cut blood vessels, and tie the vulna, and let it go until the sharpness of the splinters has subsided and the vulna has become soft, or begins to putrefy.
For blood is now flowing, then return to your operation, until you have completed it.
Then, with your finger, inquire if anything remains of the Strophuli among the others: then cut those, and clean them.
If the wen in the root of the Strophula is large, then it is necessary not to cut that Strophula from its root: rather, it is necessary to bind it with a strong thread doubled, and let it go until it falls on its own without causing any harm.
Then fill the old vulna with the Egyptian ointment that you have already submerged. Then take care of it yourself.
If the entire Strophula is cut, then it is necessary to gather the two lips of the wound together, and stitch them immediately, after which you should see that there is no surplus.
If you see that there is surplus due to the size of the Strophula, then it is necessary to consider cutting its root and taking it out, and apply the stitch I mentioned.
And if it contains humidity from the Strophula, make a superficial puncture in it: so that you can see the place of its maturity for you: and place the puncture below the body as I said.
Then apply the hair after the puncture with ointment, and similar to it, so that what remains of corruption may rot until you see the vulna already clean: then take care of it with the ointment generated by the flesh, until it is healed.
Chapter 43.
Sectioning the Epiglottis near the stoma in the throat.
The ancients performed this sectioning on the epiglottis, and I have not found anyone in our land who has done this. This is a record of their speech.
However, in those who have synchondrosis, it is necessary to avoid sectioning the epiglottis: because if there is no inflammation through this, it is because all the veins and lungs are weak.
However, in those who have hot synchondrosis in the mouth, or throat, or both, when there is no inflammation in the arytenoid cartilages, it is necessary to use sectioning of the epiglottis to avoid destruction that comes from prefecture.
Therefore, when we want to do this, it is necessary to make a small incision in the epiglottis under three circles of the epiglottis, or four, using a circular motion in the area that is between the two circles, not in the cartilage: and this is a suitable place for sectioning, because it is fatty and the blood vessels are far from it.
If the physician is timid, then it is necessary to extend the skin of the throat with a retractor. Then he finds the skin, until he becomes wet with the air: he avoids the blood vessels, if he sees anything in them.
Then he sews the sifac that we have described: and this signifies above the cut in the bronchus, when it comes out of it with that which is broken off, and by abscission of the tongue.
And release the groin at some time.
When therefore the hour comes that you fear prefecture, gather together the two lips of the skin wound, and take it alone without the cartilage.
Then administer medicines that bring forth the flesh until it is healed.
Albucasis said. The sum of this discourse, which we have related, is not an explanation, unless they understand that some of these apostemata have already weakened the infirm gullet: and the weak one has risen above death, and desires to be separated from the pain of its death: they apply to cut the epiglottis, so that the weak one may breathe above the place of the wound with a certain breathing, and be saved from death: and for this reason they were commanded to leave the open wound unstitched, until the malice of the disease has consumed it, and the malice of the disease is three days old, and almost itself: then, therefore, they were commanded to close the open wound and care for it, until it is healed.
And that which I saw through me, that one maid received a sword and sent it with her throat, and it fell with her into the part of the lung's canal.
And I was called to care for it, and I found it hissing, as is the hiss of the dead.
Therefore, I removed the wound from the gut, and found blood that had issued from the small wound. Therefore, I was confident that it had not closed the wound, nor cured it: and the air was escaping from the wound.
Therefore, I quickly applied to it and cared for it, until it is healed: and nothing happens to the maid, unless there is a rushing in the throat: and she returned after days to a better disposition of herself.
Therefore, I say that there is no fear in the section of the epiglottis.
¶ About the Section of Gut Hernia.
Head XLIII.
This Hernia of the Neck is a large ailment, according to the color of the body: and it is very common in women.
And it occurs in two ways: either it is natural, or it is accidental.
Certainly not in the natural case.
The accidental one is according to two modes: one of which is similar to small pendulous tumors. The other mode is similar to the hernia that occurs from the nodulation of the artery. And there is fear itself, and it is not proper to make an assumption about it with iron, unless it is in the small one: and you examine it yourself, and investigate it when you insert. If then you find it similar to the small pendulous tumor, and it is not suspended with any strings: then dry it, as is done with the nodules: and remove it along with whatever is contained in the purse, if it is in the purse: and if not, then examine the whole of it. Then take care of the place with what is necessary for healing until it is cured.
Head XLV.
§ On the Section of the Species of Nodules.
There are many species of nodules, and I have already mentioned all the species of these in division: and it is necessary to point out the difference between the nodule and the exit: as there is a doubt about it.
I say that when the exit is heat, and fever, and severe pains, until the ebullition of the superfluous boiling is extinguished, and the putridity is completed: then the fever and heat are quiet.
But when the nodule is not heat, nor fever, nor pain, and it contains them in the purse of sifachin which is their own sack, and it is according to the color of the body: and it is like the chestnut, and it is like the hatchet, and it is greater and smaller.
They are of two kinds: either they are fatty, or they retain moisture. The colors of moisture are many, as I said in the division.
Therefore, when dealing with swelling for treatment of Nodi, you should first try it out and then look into the instrument called Intromissive, according to its form in the chapter that follows this one.
And the method of inspection is as follows for all Nodi: take this instrument and insert it into a moister place that you find in the apostemate: and then rotate your fingers with it gradually, until you know that the instrument has penetrated the skin. Then take the last hand of yours according to the measure of the apostemate's size.
Then take out the Intromissive and look at what goes into the wound.
If it runs out with moisture of any color, then cut it off at the surface section, according to what I said in the others apostemates.
And if it does not run out with moisture in the wound of the Intromissive, then you know that it is fatty. Then cut off the section with a cross-shaped form, according to the form I showed you: and suspend it with thongs, and exfoliate the skin from all parts with ease: and guard the kistin if you can, so as to take out the healthy one with the Nodi.
But if the kistin is broken at the operation and it is not possible to take out the healthy one, often this happens, then take it piece by piece until nothing remains of it.
For if a little remains of it, or much, the Nodi return according to the most.
If it does not heal you, and there remains a little of it: then fill the wound at the completion of your operation with some sharp-edged children's thorns, and tie them up, and put above it the hot apostemate, and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
If then the knot is large, then its two lips, and care for it with it that it perishes.
If then the contrary evil is a small one, or not small: then at once, and fill the place with a sharp point, and release it tightly for two days, or three, until the wound putrefies, and rests in the ebb of the blood: then return to incise the remainder of that knot.
Chapter 46.
¶ About foreign instruments for cutting and perforating.
Of these there are three kinds: and they are of three species.
For these are large, and one is medium, and one is small.
Let them be made of steel quadrants, with sharp ends, so that they may quickly enter the apostemates.
And these are the forms of instruments for exploration and no, that is, for perforating: and one of them is called borer, that is, a piercer: and they are of three species.
For these are large, and one is medium, and one is small.
They come together, so that they may explore through them the apostemates, and exits, and fistulas, and bones from which it is between them.
And others are round, thin, soft, like a large needle, which sit on carpets, either of citrine, or of air, or of iron, or of silver.
And the better of these are those which are made of citrine.
And they are also instruments of lead black, which come together so that they may explore the fistulas, whose reflectivity is such that they reflect with the lenity of their own reflections.
There are indeed three kinds again. For they are either long, or medium, or short, according to the size of the fistula and its stricture.
The form of the ninth, and they are many kinds.
For there are among them simple ones, that is, those of a single stricture: and they are three kinds as you see, the Great, the Medium, and the Small.
And there are among them the blind of the ninth: and they are three kinds.
And there are among them the ones with two strictures: and they are three kinds: and there are also those with three strictures: and all of these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of the scalpel blades, by which the roots of the thorns, and the spines are cut off and stripped: and they are three kinds: for there are among them a great, a medium, and a small one.
Their extremities by which the section is made are sharp, while their other extremities are not sharp: and they are not placed thus, except when with them there is a stimulus for the stripping of the thorns in fear of the incision, or of the nerve: and so that it may heal by these, and find tranquility rather than what it finds at the stripping of the spines.
They are made of metal, and they are like the Rhodium, when alcohol is made: and at the wide end there is a hidden point of Spatumilis: and it runs to the inside and the outside, whenever you wish, just as you see.
The form of the Spatumilis which is hidden between the fingers at the time of the spine stripping: and they do not perceive it with the weak: and they are three kinds, a great, a medium, and a small one.
The three kinds of winds that are cut off with blood flow are: the large, medium, and small ones.
May they be made from air or saffron, round, and of about the same length as you see, and they should be fine.
And it is necessary that these kinds of winds be at your disposal: the large and small ones, so that you can cut off blood flow with them in case of need, and then when there is no medicine present.
However, you will not use them in all parts of the body for blood cutting, and you will only use them in places where there is flesh: such as the thighs, hips, shoulders, breasts, mammary glands, and vaginas, and urethras, and groins, and similar parts, from the thighs of flesh, moist.
And sometimes they become small instruments of the same kind as the fistulas of the flesh, according to their shape: which cut off blood when it flows from the site of phlebotomy, or at the incision of the vein, or artery: and sometimes they become round according to this shape.
Chapter 47.

Sometimes the breasts of some men swell up when they reach the complement of sleep (that is, when they start to pollute in sleep) until they are like the breasts of women: and they remain infected with the poison.
Therefore, if he abhors this, it is necessary to apply the moon's section to the breasts according to this shape from the line b to the line g, and then to rub off the grease entirely. If the incision does not cover the part that needs to be cut because of weakness or due to the flow of blood: then it should be filled with a wound ointment under the scalp, and released until the remaining part is cut by dryness. Then care for it until it heals.
¶ Regarding the puncture of the stitch, which happens under the Titillus.
Head 48.

Head 49.
¶ Regarding the section of the abscess that occurs due to the artery and vein.
When the artery is torn and the skin that is above it consolidates, a great abscess often occurs thereafter: and so does the vein also, as does the inflammation in that abscess.
And the signs by which it is known that the abscess and inflammation are due to the artery and vein are: for when the abscess is due to the artery, it is long, gathered in the deep part of the body; and when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel as if there is a cracking in it.
And that which is due to the vein is round in the manifest part of the body.
And the section above this abscess is an error, and particularly that which is under the scales, and in the groins, and in the neck, and in many parts of the body: and it is a great pain. Therefore, it should be neglected with iron, and that even if it is in the extremities or at the head, it should be neglected.
Therefore, above that which is from the inflammation of the artery's opening, find in the skin section in length. Then open the section with the rings, then the artery: and free it from the clothes, until it is exposed.
Then insert the knife under it, and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the artery with double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in the extraction of two arteries that are in the temples.
Then press the place which is between the two ligatures with sand, until all the blood that is in it comes out, and dissolves the aposteme.
Then apply the dressing which generates pus, until the ligatures fall: then cure it with suitable ointments until it heals.
If it is an aposteme due to the section of the vein, then it is necessary for you to hold your hand with which you can possibly take out the aposteme with the skin. Then insert the knife under the place where you held with your hand, and make it penetrate: and there should be a double thread in it, until it is taken out from the other side. Then tie the aposteme with the same good ligature: according to what I told you in the good gauze ligature, with two parts from two ends of the thread.
If however you fear that the thread will be taken out, then insert the knife another one with another thread completely at the incision of the needle: press, and tie your threads in four places.
Then cut the aposteme in the middle of it, until when it comes out that is in it: then cut the excess skin, and let what is tied out from it.
Then put on top of it a little ointment which you dipped in the wine. Then apply the dressing which is made with laver and ointments until it heals.
Caput L. (This is the Latin term for "Chapter L".)
De apostemate quod accidit ex torsione Neruorum.
Sicut accidit apostema in Arteria et Vena, similiter accidit apostema in Neruis: quod accidit in eis percussio, aut accidit a labore superfluo, et similibus: et fit plurimum illis in locis adiutoriorum, aut calcanei, et in omni loco in quo mouentur iuncturae: et est apostema graue.
Similatur color eius reliquo corpori, et est in pluribus dispositionibus absque dolore: et quando stringitur cum uehementia, sentit in eo infirmus simile stupori.
Et non est apostema aggregatum in profundo corporis, imo est sub cute, et ipsum mouetur ad omnem partem, et non uadit ad anteriora, uel ante, neque retro ad posteriora.
Quod ergo ex eis est in iuncturis, non oportit ut inuadatur cum ferro. Fortasse enim accidet contractio.
In illo autem quod ex eis est in capite, aut in fronte, finde cutem cum spatumili. Si ergo est apostema paruum, tunc tene ipsum cum forficibus, et abscinde ipsum a radice.

Head LXIX.
¶ On Castration.
Knows that castration is forbidden by our law: and for this reason I would not remember it in the book of this: and it is not necessary to remember it unless for two reasons.
One is, that it should be known by the physician when he is asked about it, and to know the treatment of the one who undergoes it.
And the other reason is, that we often require castration of certain animals for our purposes, such as sheep, horses, and goats, and similar animals.
I say, that castration is done in two ways. Either by attrition. Or by cutting and sectioning.
In those that are made by attrition, the operation is: that we make the animal sit in hot water, until the testicles of it are softened and relaxed, and hang down: then we grasp them with your hand, until they are resolved and do not appear under touch.
In castration by cutting and sectioning, it is necessary to hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspender, and dry it over the entire cut once, until the two wounds have come out: then make an incision after you have cleaned it, neither letting anything else hang on it, than the thin sifac which is under the wound.
This method of castration is better because it is done by attrition: for attrition may leave something in the testicles, therefore the animal desires copulation.
Then take care of the thigh, until it heals.

Chapter 78.
Doctrines of Midwifery, how they treat fetuses from birth, according to a non-natural figure.

For sometimes the embryo comes out of its feet, and it comes out of the body of it before the head of it, and the feet and hands of it, and one foot: or the head of it and the hand of it: or the forehead of it and the hand of it: or it comes out by the belly: and perhaps it turns over on its chest, and such like from unnatural figures.

If both hands of the fetus come out first, then it is necessary to gently reduce them with some difficulty. If she does not obey during the introduction, then place the woman on a bed, and raise her feet: then press the bed on the ground: and hold her so that she does not fall during the shock.
If the hands do not come out, and the fetus dies: then cut off the hands, and extract the remaining fetus: and tie the hand of the fetus with a cloth, and take it out with equality: for it will also come out.
The exit of the embryo from its foot. When the fetus comes out of its feet, then it is necessary to push them up: then turn the fetus slightly: and finally hold it.
Then take one of its feet, and extend it slightly.
When they come out until the thighs, then press on him to swallow it, and make it stupefy him with condiments: for he will come out if God wills.
And if he does not come out with him as we have told you, then gently reduce the fetus slightly until you place it according to the natural figure. He will then go out easily.
If anything is forbidden to go with him, take some highly alkali ointment, and then some bitter oil, and some dissolved gum: mix them all in the mortar by good percussion, and then apply a line of it to the woman's vulva, and below her ventricle. Then make her sit in warm water until she gets drowsy.
When you see that the lower parts of her are already heated, then apply some myrrh to it, and put it on. When she has held the ointment for an hour, then make her sit on a seat. Then make her snort: and draw up her nose and mouth, and press on the lower part of her ventricle by easy pressure. For the fire will go out immediately.
Exit of the fetus on the thighs and hands. When she goes out according to this form, then let her insert her hand slowly into it. Then the woman will lie down on her neck, and her feet should hang down, and she should lie down on the bed, and fold her hands. Then press on her ventricle by easy pressure. Then take out what is under her feet from the clot, until it is ready in the lower part. If the fetus does not go out, then take her feet and move them with a strong movement. Then press on what is above the drowsiness by easy pressure, until the fetus goes up to the upper part. Then let her insert her hand slowly, and press on the fetus, and tell the woman to hold it until the fetus goes out.
The exit of the fetus hanging freely from the hands. It is ingeniously reduced in its hand. However, if it cannot be reduced, then make the woman walk, and let her walk.
If however she cannot walk, then make her lie down on the bed: and strike her thighs with a violent blow.
Then apply the liniment you have prepared from mucilages that you have.
If however she accepts it, then make her sit on the seat. Then carefully reduce her hand, and evenly grasp the fetus according to its natural figure, and make her compress herself, and tell her to hold tight until she exits.
The exit of the fetus over its own neck, with its hands expanded, and its face towards the back of her mother's. It is necessary that the midwife hold onto the hand of the fetus, then gently roll it, and ease it with facility.
When it is eased, then place on top of its navel that we have mentioned from oil and mucilages.
Then tell her to move gently. When you have done that, then make her sit on the seat, and tell her to lean towards the right side. Then tell her to compress: and make her hold tight with a pinch.
The exit of the fetus prepared on the side. When it descends to the mother's opening according to this method with the second, then cut the second with your nail, until it is dry from moisture.
If however it is hung over the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel: so that it may not be held, and it may die.
Then push the fetus inside, until you place it according to what is appropriate: and tell the woman to clasp herself several times: for he himself will go out by the left side.
Exit of twins or of many fetuses. You know that twins are born frequently: and sometimes three, and four. However, that is extraordinary and rarely happens.
Five is indeed beyond nature and do not live together: and they contain them, however many there may be, in one first: and they are separated by the finger, distinguishing between them tied in the umbilicum of each of them.

If some of them are difficult at the time of parturition and go to the place we mentioned by figures, then care for them as we have said: and let it be due to the subtle thief, and do what it does with facility and tardiness, and act according to every figure with the one who is prepared for him from his ingenuity to salvation.
Remembrance of this which is formed in the womb from embryos, and are aborted.

That is done by the measurement of the glorious wise man.

Chapter 76.
Chapter on the Extraction of a Dead Foetus.
When you are treating a dead fetus, as I mentioned earlier in the division regarding medication, and it does not leave, and you force it to be operated on with your hand, then it is necessary to consider this.
If the woman is of sound constitution and has not been affected by any of the accidents that are feared to cause her miscarriage, then it is necessary for the woman to be laid on a bed, on her back, with her head lowered, and her legs raised. The attendant should hold her from two sides or lie her down on the bed so that her body is not withdrawn during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the woman's mouth with oily, high-quality oils, such as beeswax and flax seeds.
Then the midwife should anoint her hands with these oils and beeswax, and then insert it into the woman's mouth with ease. Then she will look for the place where she will make the knots from the fetus, and a suitable place for that.
Therefore, consider now if the fetus is prepared to descend on its own head, then make knots in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its shoulder, or in nearby costal regions, and under the hip bones.
If the descent is on its feet, then in the chest and in the ribs of its middle.
And it is necessary for her to hold the knot with her right hand: and she should place the fetus between the left fingers of her hand: and she will insert it with her hand with ease, and make a knot in one of those places that I mentioned, until it reaches the womb.
Then he shapes another bristle opposite it, or a third one if needed, so that the contraction is equal and does not extend to a part.
Then it is extended with an equal extension, and not just along the straight line, but it should also move to all parts so that its exit is as desired, just as happens when a tooth is removed during its extraction.
And it is necessary for there to be something in that part so that the extension is softened. If that part is held on, then it is necessary for the midwife to apply some oily fingers to it and to insert them from the side so that they rotate with the one being held.
If the part of the fetus is about to come out, then the bristles should be shifted to another place that is higher up: do this until the whole fetus has come out.
If the hand is about to come out before the other, and it cannot be reduced because of its constringence: then it is necessary for the cloth to be wrapped around it. Then remove it when it starts to come out completely, either by cutting it or in the joint of the finger, or in the elbow: and it is necessary for you to do the same with the other hand, and in two feet.
If the head of the fetus is large, or there is a constringence in its coming out, or water is aggregated in its head: then it is necessary for the midwife to insert between her fingers the Spatumile spindle, and to find the head with it and to draw out the water: or she may break it with the instrument called Almisdac, whose form comes with the forms of the other instruments in the head that follows.
Similarly, if the fetus is large-headed in nature, then it is necessary for her to push with the amniotic fluid: or she may take it out with the misdach, as I have said. Then he takes the bones with his forceps.
If he goes out the head, and bends at the shoulder: then it is found, until the moisture that is in the chest is expended.
But if he does not bend, nor yield to the exit: then he will break the head piecewise, according to what is possible for you.
If it is below the chest, or there is moisture in it: then it is necessary to pierce it, until the moisture flows out of it.
But if the fetus is above its own feet: then the attraction of it is easy, and the direction of it to the bone of the mother is light.
But if it is bent at the chest, or the breast: then it is necessary to take it out with the cloth that you have covered over your hand: and find the chest, or the breast, until the moisture that is in them flows out.
But if the remaining parts are removed, and the head returns: then the midwife inserts her left hand. Then if the bone of the mother is open: then she inserts her hand into the bone of the mother, and seeks with it the head, and draws it out with her fingers up to the bone of the mother: then she inserts a nail, or two nails, and draws it out with it.
But if the bone of the mother is bent, because of the heat that occurs to it: then it does not need to labor over it, but rather it needs at that time to administer an effusion of moist things, such as ointment: and apply the ointment: and she should sit in warm water that softens and moistens.
But if the fetus is above its own side: then it is possible for it to be equal: then the thing that I said in the fetus of the son is administered.
If that is not possible, then it is fractured in pieces and extracted.
And it is necessary to not let anything escape from the inside at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what I said about hot apostemats which occur in the womb.
If there is a flow of blood, then it should descend into warm applications, and the remainder of the treatment should be given.
And I myself have already seen a woman, in whose womb the fetus had died, and then she was impregnated on top of that, and later another fetus died as well. It happens to her after a long time, an apostemat in her belly button, which has swelled, until it is opened, and she begins to emit pus.
I am called to her treatment, and I have been treated for a long time: and the wound is not closed.
I then applied some strong attracting ointments over it: and the bone came out of its place. Then there passed some days, and another bone came out. I was amazed then, because there is no bone in the womb.
I thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I then found the bone and extracted many bones from the woman who was in better positions at the time: and she has already done so for a long time, and sends out a little pus from its place.
And I did not hold this foreign thing firmly, unless there is knowledge in it, and an aid to the doctor who performs the treatment with his hand from the cure.

About the necessary forms of instruments in the extraction of the fetus.
The form of the Vertigo that opens the womb.
This is the form of the stricture, where the books are equalized by two equal knots at the two ends of two logs. However, this Vertigo should be made to be more slender for the stricture: and it should be made either from ebony or from the wood of the bosse.
And the thickness of all woods should be almost like two fingers: and the margin of each of them is almost one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and half, and in the middle of the two woods there are two additions of the same kind of wood, which have already been firmly fixed in both, whose length is half a palm and a little less, and the width of each of them is almost two fingers or less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the womb, so that it opens with them when you turn over the two Vertigoes.
Another form similar to this, but more slender and leaner.
It should be made from ebony or bosse wood, according to the likeness of the hammer. However, at the end of it there should be two additions, as you see here above: and the length of all the addition is almost a palm: and the width of each of them is two fingers.

Head LXXVIII.
¶ On the extraction of the second child.
When the second child is held during childbirth, then it is necessary to apply strong remedies to keep its hunger. Then make it sneeze with condiments: and tightly hold your hand on its mouth, and the nostrils of its own. If then it goes out through this, it is good.

Then make it hiss, as I have said. The second part will be easier.
If however it remains after this treatment and does not go away: then advise the obstetrician to dip her hand in oil of sweet almonds, or a strong tincture of mucilage. Then she should introduce it into the uterus and seek with it the second part. When she finds it, then take it up and extend it a little at a time.
If however it is annexed to the deep matricary, then she should introduce her hand according to what we have said until she finds the second part and withdraws it a little at a time so that the matrix does not fall on the strong attraction: in fact, it should be turned with ease to the right and left side: then add to the quantity of attraction. The matricary obeys at this point and is loosened and drawn away from the adhesion.
If the mouth of the matricary is contracted as we have already mentioned: treat it with steam and the medicine of the cauldron with herbs.
If, however, he does not proceed with the others that we have mentioned, then be careful not to tire himself out over this in the course of the repeated extractions.
Indeed, it should be that whatever is inserted into the tooth of the mother, it should be placed in the woman's house. Then apply it with the ointment of Tetrapharmacian. For it will decay it after days, and it will dissolve, and it will be withdrawn.
Indeed, when it decays, it should be leeched with that bad smell to the stomach and head, and it will hurt the weak one. Therefore, it should be that the suffumigations suitable for that are administered.

Chapter 80.
¶ About the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
Fistulas which occur in the lower part are Nodules and Enlargements which occur near the deformed anus: or in a single part of one part: it is either a single fistula or several.
When that nodule becomes old, it opens, and white moisture or thin pus comes out of it.
And sometimes there are penetrating ones from these fistulas. Therefore the penetrating ones are known by that which comes out of evacuation, and moisture, when it is used in weak evacuation: and perhaps it comes out from those wombs.
And they are fistulas when they are in the space of penetrating ones until to the ute and to the virgin's meatus. And they are penetrating until to the joint of the thigh, and to the nodule of the tail.
From that by which it is known that the fistula is penetrating to the anus, and even not penetrating, is, that you put your finger into the anus: and you put your finger into the subtle one into the fistula from air or iron: when there is no tortuosity.
And if there is tortuosity in it, then you put into it a finger tentam from the knee subtle, or a pilum from the hair of horses, until you feel the tentam, or a pilum in your thumb.
If you do not perceive the whole truth, nor does anything come out of the hole, nor breath, nor offspring as I said: then you know that it is not penetrable: therefore for the treatment.
When the fistula is penetrable up to the bladder or to the urinary sediment: then its meaning is the exit of urine from it, and its prohibition for this so that the place can be healed with medicines.
If indeed it is penetrable up to the hip joint, or to the knee: then its sign is that it may pass through and try until it comes out, if there is no tortuosity up to the knee: and an finding of pain in the circumference of the part, and that pus always issues from it: and that it does not please in it any medicine, nor is it consolidated with ointment.
And in all these fistulas that are penetrable, there is no cure at all: and the cure of them is a labor and shame to him, from whom it is made.
In those however which are not penetrable and not old, hope for a cure with a bandage: according to what I tell you, and I have proved it: and it is that you lie weakly between your hands on his back: and extend his thighs above his hip bones, and his hips are inclined towards his belly. Then he will introduce the introducer into the fistula if there is tortuosity in it, until you know where it may pass.

Head 81.
¶ About the suture of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows from their incision: and care for the cuts.
There are two types of varices. Or they are within the anus, resembling carbon or prunes, or almost like grains of salt. And among them are small and large ones, and blood runs constantly from them, it is always the same, and there are many of them. And they are outside the anus and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are of few moistures, from which water white runs, or a little blood flows continuously: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of it that is inside the anus is like that of a weak person who has been beaten with an ass's hide: and it is expressed until it goes out of the anus, and becomes visible to you. Therefore, also suspend them with gut or hold them with your own grease. Then cut them at their roots.
If they are not held by the gut, because of their moisture and their own softness: then take them with a rough cloth, or with a brush made from wool, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them, and apply some warm ointment to them after cutting, so that they hold their place at the site of cauterization. Or cauterize them according to what is prescribed in the chapter on cauterization. Then take care of them with the rest of the treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not yield to the exit of the stool, then apply a weak ointment in which there is a small biting in the clister, so that it may be easy to expel with what is inside the anus, and it will yield quickly when it is expelled.
If however the warts are outside the anus, then they are easier to remove, more accessible: and it is best to capture them with your nail, or with a razor, and cut them off. Then take care of them in the manner we have said, until they heal.
And if someone dislikes cutting with iron, then it is necessary to apply a suture to them according to this method. Take the thread enveloped in the wart, and insert it into the anus. Then remove the wart from above, and make it penetrate with the needle into the root of it from the other side: and envelop the two ends of the thread with the point of the needle in the lower part, making them parallel: and fasten the wart firmly. Then cut the thread, and remove the wart.
Do this with all the warts, and let one out of them: nor take your own, lest it causes a surplus of blood from that one.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose or cinnamon oil on the anus, and place the wart on top of it: and instruct the patient to remain still. Then let it fall off, until it falls off.
When the warts fall off, take care of them with ointments and further treatment until they heal.
¶ Regarding the treatment of Fissures. Indeed they often occur due to the dryness of the feces and the constriction of nature.

Then take care of them until they are consolidated according to what is appropriate.
If they do not consolidate, then repeat them with a more severe reasoning than the first, until they bleed much and then let them care for them until they heal.

¶ About the treatment of Zuchi and Fistulas.
You know that every gallstone, or abscess when it becomes old and antiquated, and turns into a sore, and does not consolidate, and always emits pus, and does not abscess: then we call it universally in whatever member it may be, and we call it Zuchemen.
And a fistula indeed is according to truth, a filtered node, hard, white: with which there is no pain, of which the feather-like bend is connected: and for this reason some call it Risati, that is, the feather.
And it is in certain hours moist, which emits pus. And perhaps the moisture is divided in certain hours. And sometimes this moisture is much, and is little: and it is thick, and it is subtle.
And I have already predicted the division, then when I said wound, that every sore which does not heal, and is not born in the flesh, is not this but for one cause of causes.
Of which one is, either because of the scarcity of blood in the body: or because of its malice: or because there is hard and dry flesh between it and the lips of it, preventing the birth of flesh: or because it is full of sordidness and shame: or because the sore is putrid within itself, and the matter which is sent to it is of bad quality: or because the medicine is inconvenient in its cure: or because the decaying falls in the region is a kind of pestilence, or through the nature of the region, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where difficult digestion of diseases is made, and the healing of the abscess by nature is slow: or because there is one bone, or a number of bones.
I have already shown you all these causes and signs of the wounds, as well as the treatments for them with medicines in division: it is necessary for me to show you now how to make you know the treatment of fistulas and abscesses, which are made by a vascular operation with the hand.
Therefore, you should know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body. For example, there are fistulas that infiltrate into the great veins and arteries, or nerves, or tendons: or into the intestine, or into the urethra, or into some part of the ribs: or into some part of the joints composed of bones: such as the hands and feet: and they infiltrate into the proximity of the main member, and so on.
Therefore, from these fistulas, it is according to this manner that they are difficult of cure, and do not receive treatment, and the occupation with them is labor and ignorance.

¶ Of the cure of Sinu, and the quality of dressing with ointments.
When an abscess occurs in certain parts of the flesh, and it lasts for a long time until the pus collects: then it either ruptures or is perforated, and it goes out what is in it, and leaves a watery place as if it were sweat: and the skin which is over it is like fine linen which has been washed: and it does not come to the end of corruption in its own self, nor does it press into the mouth, nor into the tendons, nor into the ligaments: rightly it is called Sinus: and it is not called Fistula: but if it lasts for a long time until it presses corruption into something of these parts, then it is called Fistula, or Zuken.
And the care of it is to cut through that whole skin as much as possible: and especially when it has been made fine and smooth, like linen: and I am confident that it will not stick to its place on account of the corruption.

But that which is above the opening of the cavity, is the one that moves every hour, so as to go out that which is collected in it from the pus: and so you may know whether that which runs out from it is much, or little: or digested, or not digested.
And when you again consider the place of the cavity of that member, whether the lord of it feels pain in it, or there is no pain in it, or whether there is an apostematic swelling in it, or not.

¶ Of the cutting of the Vice.
The veins are entangled, thick, full of superfluous melancholic disorders that happen in many parts of the body: and the most common of them is in the legs, especially in the legs of those who walk and labor, and carry.

The treatment of these, when iron is used, is according to two methods. Their wounds are to be cured so that blood is drawn, and black blood is extracted. And another method is to make the vein rise and draw out all of it.
The section of this is according to this method. The thigh is first embroccated with hot water, until the thick, feces-like blood is dissolved. Then tie the weak thigh from the upper part of the hip to the lower part of the knee. Then shave the wound in one place, or two, or three wide sections.

Then tie the nail: and command him to abstain from food that produces black bile: and repeat the evacuation and phlebotomy when the veins are full, and do not harm the weak one.
The extraction of this is according to this method. Rub the weak thigh if there are many hairs in it. ¶ About the cut for the illness of Nakir.
This disease is called Nakir in our land: and it is a pain that happens in some members, and then it is changed from one member to another.
And I myself have seen it, according as I tell you. I am called to an old woman in some houses. And she takes off her arm, and I see a small inflammation in the flesh of her arm.
And after an hour she has passed, I see one inflammation going up with the fire, as if it were a child going up to her shoulder, which is higher than it can be: so that it is like silver running from place to place.
Therefore the pain has departed from that place, and it has been fixed in the shoulder.
Then I sat an hour, and it ran into the rest of the body, until it had inflamed another arm.
Then she told me that it was moving in all her body, according as I saw.
Therefore I was amazed at the rapid change of its member to another. And I myself had not seen this disease in my eyes in this manner before. Nevertheless I have seen many who found the pain to change from one member to another, and I did not see it as I saw it in the woman.
I do not think this to be the case, unless it is because she was one of those who were detected by the dry parts of the body as being of the nature of the ovary: hence it appears to the senses that her soul has been changed.
It is necessary that they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and in the moist bodies of the hidden ovaries.
When you are treating her and she feels the pain of that: then if it is apparent to you with your eye, as we have said, then tighten above it, and below it quickly: and dry above it, until it leaves that attached soul: and cauterize the place.
If you do not see it with your eyes: then treat it with the movement of the body, and with that which expels the souls, and with those that carve them with the foul pills, and the pills of serapin, and such like.
Regarding the extraction of the Sagittarius:
The Sagittarius is diversified according to its species and the locations where it falls from the body.
The diversity of theirs is: for out of them are those which have great and small points, and sharp ones, and soft ones. And out of them are those which have three angles. And out of them are those which have tongues. And out of them are those which have stars.
Those which are according to the parts where they fall, are according to two modes. Or if the parts be from the principal parts, as the brain, and the heart, and the liver, and the lungs, and the kidneys, and the intestines, and the uterus, and such like. When therefore it falls into any of these members, and you see signs of death which I will tell you later, then it is necessary for you to make an extraction of that arrow from them, for death follows the part in which it is, in many different ways. And when you do not see these signs of evil, and the arrow is not hidden deep in the member, then take out the same, and care for the groove.
For when the arrow falls into the brain, and pierces the mouth, and comes out of the siphon which is over the brain, it is: for there happen from that wound, a coma, a scotomy, a trembling, a redness in the eyes, an inflation, a red tongue, a spasm, a mixture of the intellect, and vomiting of choler. And perhaps blood will issue from the nostrils, or from the ears. And perhaps the speech is abscised, and the voice is destroyed. And there issues from the wound site, a white humidity similar to pus. And it issues from there, like water of flesh.
If then you see these signs, then abstain from treatment, and remove the arrow if it does not issue.
However, the signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are: that it is near the left breast: and it feels as if it is fixed in a hard thing, not in a soft one. And perhaps the arrow has a motion similar to that of the pulse: and it runs from the groove black blood. And it follows that cold at the extremities, and a cold sweat, and syncope. Therefore you know that death has come far from doubt.
When the arrow pierces the lung, blood starts to spurt from the wound, and the surrounding tissue becomes red and swollen. He exhales a large, high breath, seeking the cold air's attraction.
If the arrow falls into the heart, which is in the chest: then it is near the ribs: and there is a great sighing with painful breathing, with a sigh: and all the limbs of the shoulders are moved.
And if the arrow falls into the stomach: perhaps something undigested from food will exit through the wound.
And if the arrow falls into the belly, and is embedded in it: something fecal will exit through the wound, or dung, or already split intestine. There is no hope for its cure, nor in removing the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder, and urine exits: and something comes out from it to the outside, and the pain is more severe on the weakest part: then you know that it is mortal.
The remaining parts, such as the face, neck, throat, windpipe, support, and vertebrae of the back, and the knee, leg, and foot, are healed according to various dispositions: when the arrow does not hit an artery or nerve, and there is no venomous arrow.
And I tell you that I have seen these arrows, so that you understand through this about your cure.
That is, because an arrow fell into the tearful eye of a certain man, at the root of his nose. Therefore I drew it out from the other side, under the fat of his ear: and he was healed, and it did not harm him in his eye.
I extracted another arrow from a Jew, which fell into the fat of his eye beneath his lower eyelid: and the arrow was already hidden, and I could not catch it from its tip except with the very tip of my finger, where it adhered to the wood of the bow: and it was a large arrow from the bow of the Turcomen, with a soft iron, in which there were no ears.
Therefore the Jew is healed, and there does not happen to the eye of his an accident evil.
And I extracted another arrow from the throat of a Christian.
And it was an Arabian arrow, and it is this to which they have ears. Therefore I held it above the same two guides: and it was already under the throat of his. Therefore I was able to touch it with it, until I extracted it: and the Christian is healed.
And I extracted another arrow from the urine of a man, which fell into the belly of his: and we thought that he would die from it.
After thirty days had passed, and nothing had changed in his situation, I held it above the same arrow: and I touched it with my fingers, and extracted it: and he was healed, and there did not happen to him an accident evil.
And I saw a man whose arrow fell on the back of his, and the wound was closed over it. After seven years had passed, the arrow was pulled out from the root of his leg.
And I saw a woman whose arrow fell into her belly, and the wound was closed over it, and the arrow remained inside of it, and nothing had changed in her situation, and the woman did not find any harm to herself in any of the natural operations of her.
I saw another man who had a shaft fall on his face: and the sole of his foot was healed, and he found little pain in him, and such like many others.

I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs in which they are fixed, except through two ways. Or by attraction from the place from which it entered. Or from the opposite side of the other part.
And that which is coming out from where it entered, or is an arrow proceeding into the fleshy place, and it is attracted and comes out.

If a bone is imagined to be in the way, and does not yield to your will, then release it for a few days: and then try again with attraction and motion every day until it passes.
If it does not yield to your will after several days, then it is necessary to drill holes all around the bone in that bone with a sharp point, until the arrows enlarge. Then draw it towards you and remove it.
If however, the arrow is already hidden in the body, and it is hidden and concealed from the senses: then seek it out when you attempt. If however, you feel it: then draw it towards you with some instruments that are suitable for its attraction.
If however, you cannot get over it because of the constriction of the wound, and because of the length of the arrow in the deep part: and there is no bone, nor nerve, nor vein: then find something above it, until the vein enlarges, and it is possible to remove the arrow.
If the parts that hold the ears are free, then loosely fasten the flesh all around them from every side and every part of your skill, and also the skills you cannot reach beyond the flesh of the ear, and its bending, until it separates.
When you perform the extraction of the arrow, wherever it is, then use a twisting motion of your hand with the needles to all parts, until it separates: and with the finest subtlety, so that the arrow does not break, and make it difficult for you to attract it, and its own extraction.
If you cannot remove it at once, then let it be for a few days until the putrefied parts around it are removed. Then try it again: for if it makes a contrary flow of blood, then administer what I said in the chapter of its treatment: and guard your virtue from incision, or nerve, or cord.

Then he draws it: for it is itself easy to remove.

And if not: release it for a few days: then try again until it goes out.

If the arrow is sharp-pointed, then push it with the arrow as you insert it into it. The arrow is made to point by this.
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to cut all the flesh in which the poison is, if it is possible for you to do this. Then care for it as it comes near to that.
If the arrow is falling into the heart, or into the belly, or into the loin, or into the side: and it is near to that which you touch with your nail, and it is possible for you to cut over it: then cut it, and take care not to cut into the poison, or the nerve, and pull it out.

One of them is the cephalic vein, and it is from the side of the head: and it is called the vein of the head. And the black one. And it is the median vein, and it is composed of the branch of the Basilic vein, and the branch of the cephalic vein: and it is called the great vein of the body. The use and cautions in phlebotomy. The quality and accidents of phlebotomy, which you should consider when correcting it.
First of all, it is important to know that phlebotomy is not given unless in the conservation of health, and persistence in it, and caution against the coming of diseases.
And let phlebotomy be done on one arm of three, namely the cephalic, and the black, and the basilica. And let phlebotomy be done at the beginning of spring after fasting, in truth, and in summer, and autumn, and winter after eating, when there appear signs of fullness.
And let phlebotomy be done on the first day, or on the third day, after the three hours have passed, since they have exceeded them.
However, phlebotomy that is given in diseases does not have a determined hour: but when it provokes convenience and need for it, in the night or day, and in every hour, and in every time.
And it is not necessary to let blood in children until they are fourteen years old. Nor should bloodletting be done on a pregnant woman, unless from the fourth month up to the seventh. Nor should bloodletting be done on the elderly who have already passed sixty years.
For if anyone wishes to be bled for any reason, it is necessary that he cleanse his intestines before bleeding with clean cloths, if there is much fecal matter in them: so that the veins do not attract water from the intestines superfluous and putrid substances harmful to the principal membranes.
He who suffers from dizziness caused by hunger, or nausea and vomiting, or intoxication, shall not be cured until this is removed from him. He who is weak with dropsy, or oedema.
And let him be afraid of bleeding again after suffering from colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, increased secretion of urine, frequent coitus, labor, exercise, and fasting, and all that dissolves the strength of the body or animal.
Then consider the subtlety of the humors before that, if blood is thick with food and drink, and medicines: if possible, let him do this.
Then let him take a bath, if nothing prohibits it: or exercise some exercise, to thin the blood.
And place the bleeding of him in his chest, around the third day, as we said: and let him be afraid that his chest pains on that day from all the evils of animals: such as constriction, anger, and fear: and from all the evils of the body, such as labor, penalty, and superfluousness, and like this.
And let him sit and make present things with which he has used to run his custom, from the aroma, and the smell, and the scent, and like this in quantity as possible.
Then let him sit the bleeder on a higher place than the bleeding place: then he will take his arm and let him rub it with his own hand twice or three times. Then let him tighten the ligament with the correction, and bind it twice.
And let the tightening be temperate, because when it is unequal, or through superfluity in tightening, it prevents the course of the blood: or in softening, it also prevents the course of the blood.
Then after the wound is stitched up, one should use their own hands to rub it gently until the blood flows and then make the flow of blood visible.
Then the surgeon should cleanse the wound with a little oil, properly.
Then he should place his left hand on the vein at the spot where the wound is to be made, gently, so that it does not resist the needle and the blow is avoided. For the vein is like a string that runs along the wound, and there is one that is full of blood: and when you place the wound over it, it contracts under the wound, and deceives the surgeon, and does not open the wound: and if it opens, it is tight: therefore, it is necessary for the surgeon to be firm and attentive to all things.
Then he should let go of the wound. If the vein opens from the oil alone, then that is good. And if not, then try another oil in the same place, or above it with haste: if it does not open the spot.
If it opens, or weakens, then let him release it on the next day, or two days: and do not tighten the ligament. Perhaps the hot opening will be drawn. He should not enter the bath.
Then he should repeat the wound if he likes.
If the opening is small, or runs blood thinly: and fear that it may not escape from the quantity of blood you want: then repeat the wound in the same hole according to its rightness, and add a little to the operation.
And do this with haste, before the opening is made, for the open spot is in many people at small operations.
If then you see the wound already, you will not then hesitate to deal with it entirely, for nothing excuses itself before you. And place something on the wound from ointment: for it helps to stop the course of blood. And it is better in this case than the oil itself, and than the rest of the olive.
And do the same with ointment in all your phlebotomies, where the course of blood is stopped by the prohibition of the wound: and they make this Tyrannicum alfarach, and Sagzenea, when it is placed on one of them above the place.
Blood, however, becomes thin and dissolves when it is thick.
If it happens in the place of the wound-incision, which often happens, especially to those who are not phlebotomized except by that wound, or is a small opening in the skin, then immediately and on the spot place a sponge soaked in warm water and salt above the place, and string it for an hour: for it becomes thin.
And it is necessary that you do this after the exit of the blood from the wound itself, or from another wound.
If something black or yellowish remains in the place after a day, or it becomes yellow, it will not harm you: and if you wish, place something on top of it, such as aloe, or myrrh: or something from the juice of mint, that is, calamite or similar to it.
And indeed, wounds and swellings often occur at the basilica phlebotomy.
And place your hand on it, then if you find a softness under your compression on it, then that swelling is bad. Therefore, so as to place something on top of it from what we have said. Perhaps blood from this will flow from the artery.

For it often happens that the phlebotomist knows, and he falls due to negligence.

This is indeed a harmful cold, in fact, release it, until the second vein bleeds.

¶ About Ventilation, and the quality of its use.
Ventilations are made from the corners, and from the air, and from the earth.
And ventilation indeed is made in two ways. When with scarification, and the extraction of blood: and an other is ventilation without scarification.
And this ventilation which is without scarification, is in two ways. Either it is with fire. Or it is without fire.
And the ventilations which are given with scarification, and the extraction of blood, are fourteen places of the body.
